Retailers shall indicate plainly by tags or labels on the bottles or containers or on the shelf immediately below where the containers are placed, or on an exposed sign prominently placed, the price of all malt beverages or wine exposed or offered for sale. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-3-21) 
Sec. 4-100. - Compliance with health rules. 
All retail licensees under this chapter are hereby required to comply with all rules and regulations and requirements of the county board of health, state board of health and any and all other state, federal local public health authorities. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-3-22) 
Sec. 4-101. - Drinking in specified places prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person within the corporate limits of the city to: 
(1)  Publicly engage in the drinking of alcoholic beverages. 
(2)  Engage in the drinking of alcoholic beverages upon any premises upon which an athletic contest is being conducted. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person within the corporate limits of the city to drink alcoholic beverages on the premises of any retail, wholesale, or manufacturing alcoholic beverage business or business establishment. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person within the corporate limits of the city to possess an open container or to drink any alcoholic beverage on any street, highway, park, parking lot, alleyway, or public place not lawfully licensed to sell such beverages for consumption on the premises. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for any person to discard in any manner whatsoever containers of alcoholic beverages upon the street, road, highways, alleyway, parks, parking, lots, or other public places except in proper collection receptacles provided or upon any private property. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-3-25) 
Chapter 6 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Licensing and registration of animals by local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 31-19-3; livestock running at large, O.C.G.A. § 4-3-1 et seq.; permitting dogs in heat to roam or run free, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-6; disposal of diseased, disabled, or dead animals, O.C.G.A. § 4-5-1 et seq.; dogs generally, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-1; dangerous dog control, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-20 et seq.; vicious dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-40 et seq.; animal protection, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-1 et seq.; cruelty to animals, O.C.G.A. § 16-12-4; cruelty to dogs; authorized killing of dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-5; rabies control, O.C.G.A. § 31-19-1; liability of owner or keeper of vicious or dangerous animal for injuries caused by animal, O.C.G.A. § 51-2-6. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. 
Abandon means releasing or leaving an animal on any property, public or private, with the intention of deserting the animal. 
Adequate food and water means food and water which is sufficient in amount and appropriate for the particular type of animal to prevent starvation, dehydration, or a significant risk to the animal's health from a lack of food or water. 
(1)  Adequate food means palatable, noncontaminated and nutritionally adequate food that is appropriate for the species. Adequate food does not include garbage. 
(2)  Adequate water means clean, fresh, potable water. 
Adequate shelter means a structure having three sides, a top and bottom which is suitable for the animal's size to protect it from cold, wind and rain and other elements. During cold weather, sufficient bedding inside the shelter shall be present. 
Animal means any living thing not a plant, other than humans, rodents and insects. 
Animal shelter means any facility operated by the city or in conjunction with the city or its authorized agents for the purpose of impounding or caring for animals held under the authority of this chapter. 
Animal warden or animal control officer means any person that may, from time to time, be designated or employed by the city as a law enforcement officer or agency for the purpose of administration and enforcement of the provisions of this chapter. The term "animal warden" or "animal control officer" includes any county animal control officer that is authorized to act on behalf of the city by ordinance or resolution of the city council or by agreement between the city and county governing bodies. 
Cat means any feline, regardless of age or sex. 
Cruel means causing unnecessary and excessive pain or suffering, or unjustifiable injury or death. 
Dog means any canine, regardless of age or sex. 
Inoculation against rabies means the injection subcutaneously or otherwise, of rabies vaccine approved by the state department of public health, and administered under the supervision of a licensed veterinarian and a certificate of vaccination or inoculation issued by the veterinarian. 
Jurisdiction means, for the enforcement of this chapter, the corporate limits of the city. 
Leash means a cord, thong or chain not more than ten feet in length, by which an animal is controlled by the person accompanying the animal. A retractable lead may also be used by a responsible individual if the lead is of adequate strength to control the animal. Retractable leads shall only be used in open areas. 
Livestock means cattle, horses, donkeys, swine, sheep, goats, llamas, emus, ostriches, alpacas or farm-raised deer and other such animals susceptible to use for commercial purposes, including domesticated fowl, such as chickens, turkeys, geese, ducks, guineas or other poultry. 
Owner means any person partnership or corporation owning, possessing, keeping or harboring one or more animals. An animal shall be deemed to be harbored if it is fed or sheltered for seven or more consecutive days. 
Public nuisance. An animal shall be deemed to be a public nuisance if the animal: 
(1)  Is habitually permitted to go upon the property of another person other than its owner or keeper without the express consent of such other property owner or occupant. 
(2)  Attacks or acts so as to menace pedestrians or other persons using public ways. 
(3)  Habitually barks, whines or howls in an excessive, continuous, or untimely fashion. 
(4)  Is repeatedly at large. 
(5)  Trespasses on school grounds. 
Restraint means any animal that is on a leash or at heel or beside a competent person and obedient to that person's commands, or within a vehicle being driven or parked on the streets and roads of the city, or in a fenced area within the real property limits of the owner, or invisible fence systems maintained in good working order. The primary means of restraint of an animal may not be by means of a chain, cable, rope or other stakeout or tie-out device. 
Running at large means any animal that is off the property of its owner and not under the control of a competent person. 
State Law reference— Similar definitions, O.C.G.A. §§ 4-3-2, 4-8-21, 4-8-41, 4-11-1, 4-11-12. 
Sec. 6-2. - Penalties. 
Any person violating this chapter may be punished as provided in section 1-13. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-14) 
Sec. 6-3. - Administration and enforcement. 
(a)  This chapter shall be administered and enforced by the city police department in conjunction with such city personnel as are designated by the city council or appointed from time to time by the police chief to assist the police department in its enforcement duties. City police and other city officers authorized to enforce this chapter are, for those purposes, also designated as "animal control officers" or "animal wardens" as those terms are defined in this article. 
(b)  In addition to enforcement of this chapter within the jurisdictional limits of the city, the city police department and all other persons properly appointed by the city to aid the police department in enforcement of this chapter may perform enforcement duties within Lincoln County, Georgia, to the extent authorized by, and subject to any limitation of, agreements that may be entered into from time to time by the city and county for coordinated animal control. 
Sec. 6-4. - Interference with animal control officer prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to hinder, interfere, harass or otherwise obstruct the performance of any animal control officer in the official performance of his duties as provided for in this chapter. 
Secs. 6-5—6-26. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CARE AND CONTROL[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Authority of municipalities to enact ordinances for the protection of animals, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-18. 

Sec. 6-27. - Applicability to dogs. 
This article applies to all animals, including dogs. However, with regard to dogs, the provisions of this article are supplemental and in addition to the regulations provided in article III of this chapter. 
Sec. 6-28. - Bird sanctuary; wildlife. 
(a)  The entire area embraced within the corporate limits of the city is designated as a bird sanctuary. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful to trap, hunt, molest or kill any wild bird or to rob any wild bird's nest; provided, however, if nuisance birds such as starlings are found to be congregating in such numbers in a particular locality so as to constitute a nuisance or a menace to health or property in the opinion of the mayor and council, those birds may be destroyed as humanely as possible, under the supervision of the police department, in such numbers and in such manner as is deemed advisable by the mayor and council. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful to trap, hunt, molest or kill any other wild game in the city except by order of the chief of police. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-1) 
Sec. 6-29. - Animals running at large. 
It shall be unlawful for any person intentionally or otherwise to permit any livestock, fowl, or other animal to go at large. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-2) 
State Law reference— Livestock running at large, O.C.G.A. § 4-3-1 et seq.; disposal of impounded livestock, O.C.G.A. § 4-3-7. 
Sec. 6-30. - Enclosures for animals and fowl. 
Any housing or enclosure used for the keeping of animals or fowl shall be well drained, free from accumulations of animal excrement and objectionable odors, and otherwise clean and sanitary. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-3) 
Sec. 6-31. - Adequate shelter, food, water and medical care required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, whether owner, person in possession, or any person in charge of any animal, to fail, refuse or neglect to provide such animal with the adequate shelter, necessary food and water, and necessary medical treatment for such animal. 
Sec. 6-32. - Cruelty to animals prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to overload, poison, cruelly treat, maim, tease, bruise, deprive of necessary sustenance or medical attention, ill use, deprive of shade and shelter or in any manner whatsoever, torture, kill or abuse any animal. 
(b)  No person shall abandon any animal, on any property, public or private or keep an animal under unsanitary conditions. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful to transport any dog in an open bed truck except when safely confined in a portable/transport kennel or safely restrained by a harness or tether. 
State Law reference— Animal protection, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-1 et seq.; performing cruel acts on, harming, maiming or killing dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-1. 
Sec. 6-33. - Authority to remove abused or neglected animals. 
Animal control officers shall be authorized to remove or cause to have removed to a safe location any animal that appears to be abused or suffering undue pain from abuse or neglect as may be necessary to prevent further suffering. The owner or possessor of the animal may be charged according to O.C.G.A. § 16-12-4 concerning cruelty to animals. 
Sec. 6-34. - Authority to remove animals from vehicles. 
The animal control officers may use any force reasonably necessary to remove any animal locked in a closed vehicle if the owner cannot be immediately located. The operator of the vehicle will be charged with cruelty to animals as defined in this chapter. No injunction or claim for damages may be placed against the city or its designees for this action. 
Sec. 6-35. - Motorist hitting domestic animals to make report. 
Any person who, while operating a motor vehicle, strikes or causes injury to any domestic animal shall notify the owner if known or ascertainable, as well as the police department, of the injury to and location of the animal. 
Sec. 6-36. - Nuisance animals prohibited. 
It is unlawful and a violation of this chapter for any person to knowingly keep or harbor public nuisance animals as defined in this chapter. 
Sec. 6-37. - Duty of owner in case of animal bite. 
Every owner or person harboring or keeping a dog, who knows that such animal has bitten any person, shall immediately report such fact to the police department and shall keep the dog confined pursuant to the requirements this chapter. The owner or keeper of the dog shall surrender the animal to a law enforcement or humane officer, upon demand, for examination. 
Sec. 6-38. - Keeping of nondomestic, exotic, and wild animals. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for anyone to own, harbor, or permit at large any exotic animal within the areas of the city without the written permission of the chief of police, who may impose upon the owner reasonable conditions of confinement to ensure the protection and safety of the general public. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful to purchase, sell, own, possess, or harbor any skunk, fox, or prairie dog in the city. 
Sec. 6-39. - Owner responsible for damage to property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person's animal to cause damage to another person's property. The owners of such animals shall continue to be civilly liable for any damage occasioned by the actions of their animals. Property shall include, but not be limited to, pets, livestock, vehicles, etc. 
Sec. 6-40. - Vaccination of dogs and cats required. 
Any animal owner within the city shall have his animals over three months of age, including both dogs and cats, vaccinated for the prevention of rabies in a manner approved by a licensed veterinarian and consistent with state law. 
State Law reference— Responsibility for control of rabies, O.C.G.A. § 31-19-1. 
Sec. 6-41. - Report of rabies cases. 
(a)  Every veterinarian shall report promptly to the city police department and the county health department all cases of rabies in animals treated by the veterinarian, giving the name and address of the owner and a complete description and history of the animal. Every veterinarian shall also report the names and addresses of the owner of any animals bitten by the rabid animal, so far as known. 
(b)  Any person who knows that an animal, domestic or wild, is rabid; or suspects an animal of having rabies; or knows that an animal has been bitten by a rabid animal shall promptly report the information, to the extent known, to the county health department and animal control. 
Secs. 6-42—6-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DOGS[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Dangerous Dog Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-20 et seq.; vicious dog control (Mercedes' Law), O.C.G.A. § 4-8-40 et seq.; duties of cities with regard to dangerous dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-22. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 6-71. - Vicious or diseased dogs. 
(a)  Any dog that has attacked and bitten a person or other animal without provocation or has attempted to bite a person or other animal without provocation shall be deemed a vicious dog. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to cause, permit, accompany or be responsible for the presence of any vicious or diseased dog on the streets or public places of the city or allow the dog to run on the premises of another, at any time, unless and in addition to the other requirements of this chapter, the dog shall be securely muzzled to effectively prevent it from biting any person or other animal. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-12) 
State Law reference— Registration of dangerous dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-25; muzzling and restraint, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-26; confiscation and destruction, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-27. 
Sec. 6-72. - Confinement of female dogs in heat required. 
It shall be the duty of any owner, custodian or harborer of any female dog in heat within the city, when she is left unattended, to securely confine such dog inside a building or other enclosure to prevent such dog from coming into contact with another dog except for planned breeding. 
State Law reference— Permitting dogs in heat to run free prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-6. 
Sec. 6-73. - Removal of dog feces from certain areas. 
The owner, keeper, walker or person in charge of any dog shall not permit solid fecal matter of such animal to deposit on any street, alley, or other public or private property, unless such matter is immediately removed therefrom by said owner or person in charge. This section shall not apply to a person who is visually or physically handicapped. 
Secs. 6-74—6-104. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - IMPOUNDMENT 

Sec. 6-105. - Authority to impound dogs running at large. 
It shall be unlawful for any owner or possessor of any dog to permit the dog to run at large at any time, and, if any such dog is found running at large in violation of this provision, it shall be taken up and impounded as provided in this division. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-11(a)) 
Sec. 6-106. - Duty of police department and animal control officers; records. 
Except as otherwise specifically provided in this division, it shall be the duty of every police officer and every animal control officer, if any, appointed pursuant to this chapter, to seize all dogs running at large in violation of this section and to impound such animals in the city pound or other suitable place. Upon receiving any such animal, the city pound keeper shall enter upon the records of the pound, in a book to be kept by him for such purpose, the date of impounding, and a description of the animal impounded. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-11(b)) 
Sec. 6-107. - Notice to owner. 
Not later than five days after the impounding of any animal as hereinabove provided, the owner shall be notified, or, if the owner of the animal is unknown, written notice shall be posted for five days at two or more conspicuous places in the city, which notice shall describe the animal and indicate the place and time of taking. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-11(c)) 
Sec. 6-108. - Redemption. 
The owner of any animal impounded by the city pound keeper may redeem the same by paying all the costs, charges, and penalties assessed, if any, that have accrued up to the time of making the redemption, and when the same are paid to the pound keeper, it shall be his duty to release the animal from the pound and deliver it to the owner thereof. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-11(d)) 
Sec. 6-109. - Disposition of unclaimed animals. 
When the owner of such animal or animals so impounded shall fail and refuse to pay the impounding fee and costs, the animal or animals may be sold at public auction and the proceeds of such sale applied to the cost of impounding such animal or animals under the provisions as hereinafter set forth. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-11(e)) 
State Law reference— Euthanasia of dogs and cats by animal shelters, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-5.1; disposal of impounded animals, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-9.6. 
Sec. 6-110. - Fees. 
The owner of any animal or animals that are impounded under the provisions of this section shall pay such impounding fees and further fees for the keep of such animal or animals as fixed from time to time by the mayor and council. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-11(f)) 
State Law reference— Duty to provide for care of impounded animals, lien for costs of care, and return of animals to owner, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-9.3; notice to owner of impoundment, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-9.4. 
Sec. 6-111. - Summons in lieu of impoundment. 
A city officer, at his discretion, may elect not to impound a dog or other animal found in violation of any section of this chapter, but to issue or cause to be issued a summons directed to the owner or possessor of the dog to appear before the municipal court on a certain day to stand trial for the violation of this chapter. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-3-13) 
Chapter 8 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Municipal home rule, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-1 et seq.; standards and requirements for construction, alteration, etc., of buildings and other structures, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-1 et seq.; building trade contractors, O.C.G.A. § 43-14-1 et seq.; enforcement of adopted codes, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-26; state minimum standards codes, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-21; county building, electrical, and other codes, O.C.G.A. § 36-13-1 et seq.; local government code enforcement boards, O.C.G.A. § 36-74-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 8-1. - Fire limits. 
The fire limits of the city are as designated by map or legal description, duly adopted by the city council and as amended from time to time, available in the office of the city clerk. 
Sec. 8-2. - Administration by building department and building official. 
The person designated by the city council to enforce the provisions of this chapter shall be the head of the city's building department and shall be known as the "building official". As the title is used in this chapter, the term "building official" includes the duly appointed department head and his designees, including, but not limited to the city building official. 
Sec. 8-3. - Encroachment on public property prohibited. 
Any person or corporation, contractor or builder who shall, in violation of this section, encroach upon the streets and alleys or other public property of the city, shall in addition to the penalties for violation of this section, be compelled at his own expense to remove the obstructions and to repair the streets or alleys or other public property as directed by the mayor and council. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 6-1-1(d)) 
Sec. 8-4. - Closing streets prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any owner, contractor, builder or worker engaged in the building or repairing of any structure within the city, to close the streets of the city to the passage of persons or vehicles or in any way to endanger the life or limb of passersby. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 6-1-1(e)) 
Sec. 8-5. - Water and sewer connections to be supervised by city personnel. 
No connection shall be made to the city water or sewerage system except as provided in this section. Notice of the proposed connection shall be given to the city at least 48 hours in advance of the time the connection is to be made. The water superintendent shall supervise all connections to the city water system. Connections to the sewerage system shall be completed under the supervision of the wastewater superintendent. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 6-1-1(f)) 
Secs. 8-6—8-28. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CONSTRUCTION CODES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Minimum state construction codes, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-25; enforcement of minimum state construction codes, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-26. 

Sec. 8-29. - State minimum standards and permissive codes adopted. 
(a)  The following state minimum standards codes and permissive codes, as set forth in O.C.G.A. §§ 8-2-20 and 8-2-21, are adopted by the city as though fully set forth herein, as supplemented and amended by the state department of community affairs, and as may be amended by provisions of this chapter or of this Code generally: 
(1)  International Building Code, 2006 Edition. 
(2)  International Residential Code, 2006 Edition. 
(3)  International Fire Code, 2006 Edition. 
(4)  International Plumbing Code, 2006 Edition. 
(5)  International Mechanical Code, 2006 Edition. 
(6)  International Fuel Gas Code, 2009 Edition. 
(7)  National Electrical Code, 2008 Edition. 
(8)  International Energy Conservation Code, 2009 Edition. 
(9)  International Property Maintenance Code, 2006 Edition. 
(10)  International Existing Building Code, 2006 Edition. 
(b)  Subsequent editions or amendments to the adopted publications and state amendments and errata shall become effective 30 days after the city council receives notice that copies of such publications have been obtained, unless the council within such 30-day period disapproves the subsequent edition or amendment. 
(c)  A copy of each adopted code of technical regulations, as well as the adopting ordinance, shall be authenticated and recorded by the clerk and kept on file in the office of the clerk where they shall be available for public inspection. 
Sec. 8-30. - Codes remedial in nature. 
The city's technical codes are remedial in nature, and shall be construed to secure the beneficial interests and purposes thereof, which are public safety, health, and general welfare through structural strength, stability, sanitation, adequate light and ventilation, and safety to life and property from fire and other hazards attributed to the built environment, including alteration, repair, removal, demolition, use and occupancy of buildings, structures, or premises, and by regulating the installation and maintenance of all electrical, gas, mechanical and plumbing systems. 
Sec. 8-31. - Quality control. 
Quality control of materials and workmanship is not within the purview of this Code except as it relates to the purposes stated herein. 
Sec. 8-32. - Liability of city. 
The inspection or permitting of any building, system or plan, under the requirements of this Code shall not be construed in any court as a warranty of the physical condition of such building, system or plan or their adequacy. Neither the city nor any employee thereof shall be liable in tort for damages for any defect or hazardous or illegal condition or inadequacy in such building, system or plan, nor for any failure of any component of such, that may occur subsequent to such inspection or permitting. 
Sec. 8-33. - Conflict of regulations. 
Where in any specific case sections of the technical codes, of this Code, and of state or federal law or regulation specify different materials, methods of construction or other requirements, the most restrictive shall govern. Where there is a conflict between a general requirement and a specific requirement, the specific requirement shall be applicable. 
Sec. 8-34. - Appendices to technical codes. 
Appendices referenced in the code text of the technical codes shall be considered an integral part of the codes. 
Sec. 8-35. - Referenced standards. 
Standards referenced in the text of the technical codes shall be considered an integral part of the codes. If specific portions of a standard are denoted by code text, only those portions of the standard shall be enforced. Where code provisions conflict with a standard, the code provisions shall be enforced. Permissive and advisory provisions in a standard shall not be construed as mandatory. 
Sec. 8-36. - Requirements not covered by code. 
Any requirements necessary for the strength, stability or proper operation of an existing or proposed building, structure, electrical, gas, mechanical or plumbing system, or for the public safety, health and general welfare, not specifically covered by this or the other technical codes shall be determined by the building official. 
Sec. 8-37. - Alternate materials and methods. 
The provisions of the technical codes are not intended to prevent the use of any material or method of construction not specifically prescribed by them, provided any such alternate has been reviewed by the building official. The building official shall approve any such alternate, provided the building official finds that the alternate for the purpose intended is at least the equivalent of that prescribed in the technical codes in quality, strength, effectiveness, fire resistance, durability and safety. The building official shall require that sufficient evidence or proof be submitted to substantiate any claim made regarding the alternate. 
Sec. 8-38. - Required inspections. 
The following inspections are mandatory: 
(1)  Temporary service pole. 
(2)  Manufactured home stand/tie downs. 
(3)  Footing. 
(4)  Monolithic slab. 
(5)  Foundation wall. 
(6)  Manufactured home pier footing. 
(7)  Poured wall rebar. 
(8)  MH curtain wall. 
(9)  Retaining wall. 
(10)  Concrete slab rough-in. 
(11)  Framing rough-in. 
(12)  Electrical rough-in. 
(13)  Mechanical rough-in. 
(14)  Plumbing rough-in. 
(15)  Garage/porch slab base. 
(16)  Energy. 
(17)  Temporary power on. 
(18)  Main systems testing. 
(19)  Final inspection and certificate of occupancy for move in. 
Sec. 8-39. - Building permits; fees. 
Provisions regarding building permits are included in chapter 26, Land Use. Building permits and inspection fees shall be in the amount established by the city council and included in the city fee schedule. 
Secs. 8-40—8-66. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PROPERTY NUMBERING 

Sec. 8-67. - Required; specifications; placement. 
All owners of dwelling houses or business buildings situated within the city shall place thereon numerals or numbers of sufficient size and legibility as to be easily read, the same to be placed in a conspicuous place on the front of the dwelling or business building. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 6-1-3(a)) 
Sec. 8-68. - Assignment of number by building official. 
The building official shall, upon application therefor by the owner, designate and assign a number to each dwelling house and business building in the city. After a number is assigned, the owner shall obtain suitable numbers or numerals to affix the same to his dwelling house or business establishment. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 6-1-3(b)) 
Chapter 10 - BUSINESSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— For alcoholic beverages establishment regulations and excise taxes, see Chapter 4. For hotel-motel excise taxes, see Chapter 44. 
State Law reference— Authority of cities and counties to license self-service motor fuel dispensing pumps, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-1; certain persons required to provide proof of licensure state licensure before issuance of city or county business license, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-6; limitations regarding persons performing investigations related to city and county business licenses, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-9; taxation of insurers, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-1 et seq.; licensing and taxation of certain businesses, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-1 et seq.; municipal and county occupation taxes for certain traveling salespersons, merchants, and dealers, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-354. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 10-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Administrative fee means the component of the occupation tax which approximates the reasonable cost of handling and processing the occupation tax. 
Business means any business, trade, occupation, profession, avocation or calling of any kind for gain or profit, directly or indirectly; provided that this shall not include any business, trade, profession and the like licensed by the state unless city licensing is allowed by state law, nor shall it include any business operating solely under a franchise granted by the city. 
City clerk includes the city clerk and his designees and any alternates that may be designated from time to time by the city council to enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
Employee means any individual who, for compensation, exerts substantial effort within the state for the purpose of soliciting business or serving customers or clients. 
Engaged in business. Any person shall be deemed to be engaged in business and thus subject to the requirements of this chapter when he performs any act of selling any goods or services or solicits business or offers goods or services for sale for payment in an attempt to make a profit, including the sales or services of the character as made by a wholesaler or retailer or involved in any of the functions performed as a manufacturer, either as an owner, operator or agent in any business, trade, profession or occupation within this city. 
Gross direct premiums means gross direct premiums as used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-4. 
Home repair service person means any individual engaged in plumbing, electrical, carpentry, repair or maintenance activities performed on single-family residential units located within the city; provided, however, the charges for such services, exclusive of materials, do not exceed $200.00 per residential unit per year. 
Insurer means a company which is authorized to transact business in any of the classes of insurance designated in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5. 
Location or office means a fixed place located within the city from which a person conducts business, but does not include a work site located in the city for less than six consecutive months for the purpose of serving a single customer or project. 
Manufacturer means a person who, either directly or by contracting with others for the necessary labor or mechanical services, manufactures for sale or commercial use any articles, substances or commodities, including all the activities of a commercial nature wherein labor or skill is applied by hand or machinery to materials so that as a result thereof a new, different, or useful article of tangible personal property or substance of trade or commerce is produced, including the production or fabrication of specially or custom-made articles, and including the making, fabricating, processing, refining, mixing, slaughtering, packing, aging, curing, preserving, canning and preparing and freezing of fresh foods, fruits, vegetables and meats. 
Occupation tax means a tax levied for revenue purposes on persons, partnerships, corporations or other entities for engaging in an occupation, profession or business in the city. 
Occupation tax certificate means a document issued by the city acknowledging payment of the occupation tax and administrative fee. 
Practitioners of professions and occupations means those individuals listed in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-9(c)(1)—(18), but does not include a practitioner who is an employee of a business if such business pays an occupation tax. 
Regulatory fee means a fee which approximates the cost of regulatory activity by the city. 
Regulatory fee certificate means a document issued by the city acknowledging payment of a regulatory fee. 
Retailer means a person who sells tangible personal property to the consumer or any other person for any purpose other than for resale. 
Services means the accommodating or performing of a duty or work by a person utilizing time or talents for direct or indirect remuneration. 
Wholesaler means a person who sells tangible personal property to jobbers or to another person other than the consumer. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, §§ 7-1-1, 2-5-21) 
State Law reference— Similar definitions, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-5. 
Sec. 10-2. - Applicability of chapter. 
This chapter is applicable not only to those business entities specifically mentioned herein, but also to businesses that are the topic of other chapters of this Code. The provisions of this chapter shall be supplemental to the provisions of those other chapters to the extent they are not in conflict therewith. 
Sec. 10-3. - Subsequent amendments; other fees. 
This chapter shall be subject to amendment or repeal, in whole or in part, at any time, and no amendment or repeal shall be construed to deny the right of the city to assess, levy and collect any of the license fees prescribed. The payment of any license fee herein provided for shall not be construed as prohibiting the assessment, levy or collection of additional license or permit fees upon the same person, firm or corporation. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-21) 
Sec. 10-4. - Confidentiality. 
All information furnished or secured under the authority of this chapter shall be kept in strict confidence by the city, shall not be subject to public inspection, and shall be utilized solely by the officers of the city responsible for administering the provisions of this chapter and the city's business taxes. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-4(4)) 
State Law reference— Confidentiality of information and penalties for violation, O.C.G.A. §§ 48-13-15 and 33-8-10. 
Secs. 10-5—10-26. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 10-27. - Authority to administer chapter. 
The city clerk shall administer and enforce the provisions of this chapter for the application for and issuance of business licenses under this chapter of this Code. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-5) 
Sec. 10-28. - Duties of city clerk. 
The city clerk, or an authorized representative, shall have, among others, the following duties: 
(1)  To prepare and provide the necessary forms for the registration and application for a business license and for the submission of any required information as may be necessary to properly administer and enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
(2)  To issue to each person a business license within a reasonable time after the payment of the license fee assessed and any business taxes, property or other city taxes levied in this Code; provided, however, where under other portions of this Code, permits, certifications and compliance with enumerated conditions are required for the operation of the business, the city clerk shall not issue a business license until the applicant exhibits to the city clerk the obtained permits, certification and compliance. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-6) 
Sec. 10-29. - Violations and penalties. 
(a)  It shall be a violation of this chapter for any person, whether based in the city or elsewhere, to transact any business of a type for which this chapter requires a license, or to carry on any business for which a license is required, however briefly or however transitorily, without first obtaining a license to do so, under the provisions of this chapter. 
(b)  It shall be a violation of this chapter for any person, whether based in the city or elsewhere, made liable for obtaining a business license under this chapter, to fail to show the license or a copy thereof to any police officer within a reasonable time after the making of a demand therefor by the police officer. 
(c)  It shall be a violation of this chapter to fail to pay the license fees required by this chapter by the date on which such payments are due. 
(d)  Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall, upon conviction in the municipal court of the city, be punished as provided in section 1-13. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-18) 
Sec. 10-30. - Late payment penalties. 
(a)  Should any occupation tax or regulatory fee imposed by this article remain due and unpaid for 90 days from the due date of the tax or fees, the person liable for the tax or fee shall be subject to and shall pay a penalty of ten percent of the tax or fee. 
(b)  Any occupation tax, regulatory fee, or administrative fee which becomes delinquent shall bear interest from the date of delinquency on the unpaid amount at 1.5 percent per month or 18 percent per annum. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 301(B); Ord. of 2-6-2012) 
State Law reference— When payment due, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-20; penalty and interest on default in payment, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-21. 
Sec. 10-31. - Defense to prosecution. 
(a)  It shall be a defense to any prosecution under this chapter for failing to obtain a business license before engaging in business, that a license has in fact been issued in the manner provided by law. 
(b)  It shall be presumed that no license has been issued unless at his trial the accused produces in court his currently valid business license or a certified copy thereof. In no event shall the claim by the accused that he has been issued a currently valid business license which has been lost be sustained unless that person shall have first reported the alleged loss to the city clerk and made demand for the issuance of a new license. The report of loss or demand for issuance of a replacement license must have been made prior to the arrest for the violation for which the accused is charged. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-19) 
Sec. 10-32. - Owner and manager both punishable for violations. 
In the event that a business is being conducted without a license, both the person owning the business and the person in charge of the management of the business in the city may be held liable for the violation of the provisions of this chapter, and upon conviction, either or both may be punished as provided for in section 10-29. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-20) 
Secs. 10-33—10-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - LICENSES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 10-51. - Required. 
Every business in this city or person doing business or engaged in business within the city is hereby required to have a business license from the city for the privilege of engaging in a business, profession or occupation within the corporate limits, unless city licensing is prohibited under state law or the activity is exempted by this Code. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-2) 
Sec. 10-52. - Separate businesses. 
In the case of a business conducted at more than one store, location or place, each store, location or place shall be considered a separate business under the terms of this chapter, and a separate license shall be required for each. Should more than one business on which a business tax is levied by this Code be conducted in or in conjunction with one place or kind of business, each business shall be separately licensed under this chapter. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-3) 
Sec. 10-53. - Casual and isolated activity. 
Except as otherwise provided in this article, nothing herein contained shall be interpreted so as to require any person who may engage in casual or isolated activity and commercial transactions, which involve personal assets only and activities and transactions are not the principal occupation of the individual, to obtain a business license and pay a fee therefor. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-8) 
Sec. 10-54. - License not issued to persons indebted to city. 
No license shall be issued to any applicant who has any outstanding indebtedness to the city, including but not limited to property taxes, business license fees, business taxes, utility bills and any other taxes or assessments. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-10(c)) 
Sec. 10-55. - Applicability to transient and temporary businesses. 
Transient and temporary businesses shall pay any fees or taxes provided for in this article. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-4) 
Sec. 10-56. - Special daily business license. 
In lieu of obtaining a business license as provided in this chapter, a person not maintaining a fixed place of business in the city may obtain from the city clerk a special daily business license which shall expire at 12:00 midnight of the day for which it is issued. A new license shall be obtained for each day on which any type of business is to be conducted. Any person desiring to engage in a business licensed under this section shall obtain a license prior to engaging in business on the day for which the license is issued and pay all license fees and business taxes required under this Code. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-9) 
Sec. 10-57. - Special provisions for disabled veterans. 
All disabled veterans desiring to enter business without paying city license fees or business taxes must present a state disability license to the city clerk whereupon a city license will be issued and marked "FREE" on the face of the same. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-17) 
Sec. 10-58. - Licensing does not confer right to engage in business. 
Nothing herein contained shall be construed as granting any person whose business is subject to municipal regulation any legal right to engage in that business. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-10(g)) 
Secs. 10-59—10-89. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PROCEDURE 

Sec. 10-90. - Time for application processing. 
Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, all license applications shall be approved or disapproved within ten days of filing with the city clerk. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-10(f)) 
Sec. 10-91. - Application form; due date. 
(a)  Every person required to procure a license under the provisions of this Code shall submit an application for the license to the city clerk, which application shall conform to the requirements of this section in addition to any other provisions of this Code. Unless otherwise provided in this Code, each application shall be a written statement upon forms provided by the city and submitted before the last day of April of each year or within ten days of opening a new business or reopening of a business under a new ownership. 
(b)  Each application shall contain the following information: 
(1)  Name and home address of the applicant if an individual, or home office address if a corporation or partnership; 
(2)  Place where the proposed business is to be located; 
(3)  Kind and class of business to be carried on; 
(4)  Names and home addresses of the partners if a partnership; 
(5)  Names and home addresses of the officers and directors if a corporation; 
(6)  Any information as may be required by the city clerk for the purpose of determining the amount of any business taxes to be collected under this Code; and 
(7)  Any additional information which the city clerk may find reasonably necessary to the fair administration of this chapter of the Code, which may include a complete record of all arrests and convictions against the applicant and every partner, officer or director of the applicant for violations of any and all laws and ordinances of the city, state or federal government other than minor traffic violations. 
(c)  Each application shall be signed and sworn to by the applicant if an individual, or by a partner if a partnership, or by an officer if a corporation. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-4(1)—(3)) 
Sec. 10-92. - Evidence or qualification required if applicable. 
(a)  Any business required to obtain health permits, bonds, certifications of qualifications, certificates of competency or any other regulatory matter shall first, before the issuance of a city registration, show evidence of such qualification. 
(b)  Each person who is licensed by the state shall post the state license in a conspicuous place in the licensee's place of business and shall keep the license there at all times while the license remains valid. 
(c)  Each person or business operating within the city must show proof of a business license in the state prior to conducting business within the city. If proof is not shown, the city shall levy a fee of $100.00 for obtaining proof of said license. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 302) 
State Law reference— Municipal licensing and taxation of businesses, trades and professions licensed by state, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-18. 
Sec. 10-93. - False statements grounds for revocation. 
False statements on any application for a license shall be grounds for immediate revocation of the license or denial of the application. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-4(5)) 
Sec. 10-94. - Fees. 
Any application, license and registration fees as fixed from time to time by the mayor and council or business taxes required under this Code shall accompany the application. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-4(6)) 
Sec. 10-95. - Denial by city clerk; appeal. 
(a)  The city clerk shall review the application to ensure that it is complete and meets all requirements provided in this and any other chapters. If the application is proper, the city clerk shall proceed as provided in this division. 
(b)  If, however, the city clerk determines that the application is not in order or any requirements for the license have not been met, then the city clerk shall deny the application and immediately provide written notice of the denial and the grounds therefor to the applicant. 
(c)  The applicant may appeal the denial to the mayor and council within ten days of the denial notice being issued. The mayor and council shall hold a public hearing on the appeal within ten days of the appeal being filed with the city clerk. The mayor and council, within ten days of the hearing, may order the license granted with or without conditions or may affirm the denial of the application. The decision shall be based only upon a finding by the mayor and council that the city clerk was correct or erred in the interpretation of the regulations involved or the facts of the case. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-10(e)) 
Sec. 10-96. - Review by designated city officials. 
If any provision of this Code provides for the review of an application for a license by a city officer designated therein, the city clerk shall forward a copy of the application to that officer. The officer charged with the duty of reviewing the application shall make a recommendation thereon, favorable or otherwise, and shall return the recommendation to the city clerk after receiving a copy of the application. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-10(a)) 
Sec. 10-97. - Submission to city council. 
Upon the receipt of the recommendation of the reviewing officer, or upon the receipt of the application, if no reviewing officer is designated, the city clerk shall forward the recommendation and application to the mayor and council for consideration and action at its next regularly scheduled public meeting, if approval by the mayor and council is required. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-10(b)) 
Sec. 10-98. - Issuance. 
Upon the express approval of the mayor and council, when so required, or otherwise upon a determination by the city clerk that the application is in order and all requirements have been met, the city clerk shall issue a business license to the applicant therefor, which license shall state the nature of the business authorized and bear the date of issuance and the signature of the city clerk. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-10(d)) 
Sec. 10-99. - Display of licenses. 
All persons shall exhibit and display all licenses issued to them under this Code in some conspicuous place in their business establishment at which address the license was issued. Any transient or nonresident person, firm or corporation doing business within the city shall carry the license either upon his person or in any vehicle or other conveyance which is used in the business and the person shall exhibit the same to any authorized enforcement officer of the city when so requested. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-11) 
State Law reference— Duty to post license in place of business, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-23. 
Sec. 10-100. - Duration of license. 
Any license referred to in this chapter shall automatically expire on December 31 of the year of its issuance. Licenses issued to transient and temporary businesses shall be valid for a period of 180 days. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-7) 
Sec. 10-101. - Renewal of licenses. 
Each licensee shall make a written application for renewal on forms supplied by the city clerk no later than April 30 of each calendar year, which application may require substantially the same information as the initial application. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-12) 
Sec. 10-102. - Change of address. 
Any person licensed hereunder moving from one location to another shall notify the city clerk of the move and the new address in writing on a form provided by the city clerk no later than the day of moving. The same business license will be valid at the new location if the new location conforms to other requirements of this Code. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-14) 
Sec. 10-103. - Transfer of licenses. 
(a)  Business licenses shall not be transferable except as provided in this section. In the event that the owner of a business holding a currently valid, paid-up business license should sell or transfer the business to another person, the purchaser of the business shall obtain free of charge a new license in his name for the balance of the current term of the seller's business license upon making application to the city clerk, and the purchaser shall be punishable for violation of this chapter if the transfer of the business license provided for in this section is not made before the transferee begins to engage in the business. 
(b)  At the date of renewal of the seller's business license, the buyer must obtain a new annual business license and pay all license fees and business taxes required by this Code and comply with all applicable provisions of this Code and all ordinances in the same manner as if he had been the original owner of the business. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-15) 
Sec. 10-104. - Issuance of replacement licenses. 
In the event that the city clerk is notified that the licensee has lost his copy of the license, he shall make a new copy upon showing by the licensee that the required fees have been paid. In addition, the licensee shall be charged a replacement fee as fixed from time to time by the mayor and council. Replacement licenses shall be signed by the city clerk and shall indicate the time and date upon which issued. The possession of a replacement license shall not be a defense to any charge of violation of this chapter except a charge made after the time of the issuance of the replacement license. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-16) 
Sec. 10-105. - Revocation; suspension. 
(a)  Violations of this article or any other ordinance or regulation of the city shall constitute grounds for suspension or revocation of a business registration. The provisions and requirements of this article shall be enforced by injunctions. 
(b)  The mayor and council after affording the licensee a five-day notice of the charges and opportunity to be heard with respect to any revocation proceedings, may, if it finds this Code to have been violated by the licensee, his agent, or employee in the operation of the business, revoke any and all city licenses in their entirety, suspend the same for a specified period of time, place the licensee on probation or place other conditions thereon as the mayor and council may deem necessary after a hearing thereon. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-13; Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 401(A)) 
Secs. 10-106—10-123. - Reserved.

Sec. 10-124. - Purpose. 
Regulatory fees paid by businesses or practitioners are to defray cost for investigations or inspections of such businesses or practitioners as a protection to the public health, safety, or welfare or in the course of enforcing, a state or local building, health, or safety code. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 206) 
Sec. 10-125. - Imposed. 
A regulatory fee will be imposed as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-9 on the following businesses: 

 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 202(A)) 
Sec. 10-126. - Amendment. 
The regulatory fee schedule may be amended to add businesses or practitioners by resolution by the mayor and council as needed. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 202(B))

ARTICLE V. - OCCUPATION TAXES[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Taxation of businesses and practitioners of professions and occupations with one or more locations in a county or municipality, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-6; taxes on businesses and practitioners of professions and occupations with no location in state, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-7; prohibited practices in levying tax, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-13. 

Sec. 10-152. - Purpose and scope. 
The occupation tax levied herein is for revenue purposes only and is not for regulatory purposes, nor is the payment of the tax made a condition precedent to the practice of any such profession, trade or calling. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 206) 
Sec. 10-153. - Option to establish exemption or reduction in tax. 
The mayor and council may in subsequent ordinance or resolution provide for an exemption or reduction in occupation tax to one or more types of businesses or practitioners of occupations or professions as part of a plan for economic development. Such exemptions or reductions shall not be arbitrary or capricious and the reasons shall be set forth in the minutes of the council. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 402) 
Sec. 10-154. - Administration; director. 
The director appointed by the city council shall administer and enforce the levy, assessment, and collection of the occupational taxes imposed by this article. The city clerk and chief of police, or either of them, are designated as director for purposes of this article. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 102) 
Sec. 10-155. - Tax levy based on number of employees. 
(a)  An occupational tax is levied upon those businesses and practitioners of professions and occupations with one or more locations or offices within the incorporated areas of the city or upon the applicable out-of-state businesses with no location or office in this state pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-13-7, based upon the number of employees of the business or practitioner, as follows: 

 
(b)  The number of employees shall include full-time and full-time equivalent working for the business. A "full-time" employee is an employee who works 40 or more hours per week. Each part-time employee shall count as one-half an employee for occupational tax purposes. The owner and other family members working for the businesses, whether paid or not, shall be included in this count. 
(c)  The number of employees shall be determined by the average number of employees of a business for the four previous quarters of operation of a business year. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 201) 
State Law reference— Taxation of businesses and practitioners of professions and occupations with no location in state, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-7. 
Sec. 10-156. - Tax levy based on business location. 
(a)  Wherever a business or occupation is conducted at more than one location or place within the city, each such location shall be considered a separate business for the purpose of the occupation tax imposed by this article. 
(b)  An occupation tax is hereby levied on those businesses and practitioners of professions with no location or office in the state if the business' largest dollar volume of business in this state is in the city and the business or practitioner: 
(1)  Has one or more employees or agents who exert substantial effort within the jurisdiction of or serving customers or clients; or 
(2)  Owns personal or real property which generates income and which is located within the jurisdiction of the city. 
(c)  The city shall not require an occupation tax on those real estate brokers, agents, or companies, whose offices are located outside the city and sell property in the city. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 203) 
Sec. 10-157. - Practitioners exclusively practicing for the government exempted. 
Any practitioner whose office is maintained by and who is employed in practice exclusively by the United States, the state, a municipality or county of the state, or instrumentalities of the United States, the state or a municipality or county of the state shall not be required to pay an occupation tax for that practice. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 205) 
Sec. 10-158. - Insurance companies. 
(a)  Generally. There is hereby levied an annual license fee upon each insurer doing business within the city in the amount of $25.00. For each separate business location in excess of one not covered by subsection (b) of this section, operating on behalf of such insurers within the city, there is hereby levied a license fee in the amount of $25.00. 
(b)  Insurers insuring certain risks at additional business locations. For each separate business location, not otherwise subject to a license fee hereunder, operated and maintained by a business organization which is engaged in the business of lending money or transacting sales involving term financing and in connection with such loans or sales, offers, solicits or takes application for insurance through a licensed agent of an insurer for insurance, said insurer shall pay an additional license fee of $10.00 per location for each year. 
(c)  Insurance agency license fees; independent insurance agencies and brokers. There is hereby levied an annual license fee upon independent agencies and brokers for each separate business location from which an insurance business is conducted and which is not subject to the company license fee imposed by subsection (a) of this section, in the amount of $20.00 for each such location within the city. 
(d)  Gross premiums tax on life insurers. There is hereby levied an annual tax based solely upon gross direct premiums upon each insurer writing life, accident and sickness insurance within the city in an amount equal to one percent of the gross direct premiums received during the calendar year in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.1. The premium tax levied by this section is in addition to the license fees imposed by subsection (a) of this section. 
(e)  Gross premiums tax upon all other insurers. There is hereby levied an annual tax upon each insurer, other than an insurer transacting business in the class of insurance designated in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5, doing business within the city in an amount equal to 2½ percent of the gross direct premiums received during the calendar year, in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2. 
(f)  Due date. License fees imposed in subsections (a), (b) and (c) of this section shall be due and payable on February 1 of each year. The due date for gross premiums tax imposed in this section shall be as provided by state law. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 2-5-30) 
State Law reference— License fees of insurance companies generally, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-3; county and municipal corporation tax on life insurance companies, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.1; county and municipal corporation tax on other than life insurance companies, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2; municipal authority to impose license fee on life insurance companies, O.C.G.A. § 38-8-8. 
Sec. 10-159. - Proration for new businesses. 
When any person commences business on or after July 1 in any year, the occupation tax and regulatory fee for the remaining portion of the year will be 50 percent (or one-half) of the tax imposed for the entire year. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 301(C)) 
Sec. 10-160. - Due date. 
Except as otherwise specifically provided in this article, all occupation taxes and regulatory fees levied by this article shall be due and payable annually on January 1 and shall be delinquent if not paid by March 1. In the event that a person commences business on any date after January 1 in any year, the tax shall be due and payable on the date of the commencement of the business for that part of the year remaining. 
(Ord. of 12-1-2008, § 301(A)) 
State Law reference— When payment due, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-20; penalty and interest on default in payment, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-21. 
Secs. 10-161—10-190. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - PEDDLING, SOLICITING AND CANVASSING 

Sec. 10-191. - Registration required. 
Any person peddling, soliciting or canvassing within the city shall be required to register and obtain an identification card as provided by this article. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-2-1) 
Sec. 10-192. - Registration fee; application for identification card. 
Any person desiring to peddle, solicit or canvass within the city shall pay to the city clerk or his designated representative a registration fee as fixed from time to time by the mayor and council and shall make application with the chief of police for an identification card which shall show payment of the registration fee and the days that the registrant has registered to peddle, solicit or canvass within the city. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-2-2) 
Sec. 10-193. - Exhibition of registration card. 
Each registrant shall at all times while in the city have upon his person the registration card and shall exhibit the same when requested to do so by any law enforcement officer or by any municipal authority and by any person being solicited. Possession of this registration card shall not in any way represent an endorsement or approval of any products or project by the city. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-2-3) 
Sec. 10-194. - Unlawful acts. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to peddle, canvass or solicit after sundown within the fire zone of the city, without having registered with the city clerk in accordance with this article, or without having on his person and in his possession an identification card issued in accordance with this article. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-2-4) 
Chapter 12 - COURTS AND JAILS 
(RESERVED)
