The building official shall not issue any permit for the erection of any building or structure to be located in any subdivision, a plat whereof is required to be recorded pursuant to the provisions of these regulations, until such plat shall have been admitted to record as provided for in these regulations. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 11-6) 
Sec. 26-818. - Occupancy. 
No dwelling within the city may be occupied for dwelling purposes until all required utility installations, including water supply and sanitary sewer systems, have been completed to the satisfaction of the building official. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 11-7) 
Secs. 26-819—26-834. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - SIGNS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 26-835. - Purpose and intent. 
(a)  It is the purpose of the city council in enacting this chapter to provide standards to safeguard life, public health, property and welfare by regulating the location, size, illumination, erection, maintenance and quality of materials of all signs. More specifically, signs have a powerful impact on the aesthetic environment of the community, and it is the purpose of this article to encourage an aesthetically attractive environment, while allowing sufficient opportunities for communications to serve business and comply with the federal and state constitutions and laws. 
(b)  Signs create visual clutter and therefore should be regulated in their size, location, construction and illumination. Signs can detract from the beauty of the neighborhood and lower property values. In seeking to comply with federal and state law, the board has determined that large billboards are, as the U.S. Supreme Court has recognized, an aesthetic harm; that the Georgia Supreme Court has upheld sign regulations on the basis of aesthetics and preserving the beauty of environment; and, that the Eleventh Circuit Court has recognized portable signs are visual clutter and a potential traffic hazard. These holdings show that the city's ordinance is within the law and therefore constitutional, which is a goal of the city. 
(c)  Many signs can also be a hazard and negatively impact traffic safety, by distracting drivers and blocking views of other vehicles and dangers, by making intersections more treacherous, and by making it difficult to see oncoming traffic when entering a roadway. Therefore, it is also the purpose of this article to prevent those harms by regulating signs to safe locations, safe sizes, with proper and safe illumination and construction. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-1) 
Sec. 26-836. - Jurisdiction. 
The provisions of this article shall govern the use of all land and development within the incorporated areas of the city. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-1-3) 
Secs. 26-837—26-865. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PERMITTED AND PROHIBITED SIGNS 

Sec. 26-866. - Purpose; applicability. 
This division enumerates the signs that are permitted and prohibited in each specific zoning district, subject to standards and specifications otherwise provided in this article. If not otherwise stated, any sign not specifically permitted in a zoning district as provided under this division shall be prohibited. Any sign not visible from the outside of a structure or to passing members of the public is not regulated by this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 19-2, 19-2-2(E)) 
Sec. 26-867. - R-1, R-2, RMH and D-1 zoning districts. 
The following signs are permitted in R-1, R-2, RMH and D-1 zoning districts: 
(1)  Ground signs. Permitted grounds signs are limited to one single-face sign per lot having an occupied residential structure with a maximum size of six square feet, a maximum height of six feet above ground level, and a maximum width of six feet. Illumination of ground signs shall be governed by general ground sign illumination standards as provided in this division. 
(2)  Window signs. Permitted window signs are limited to one sign per dwelling with a maximum size of four square feet; provided, however, that window signs may not cover more than 25 percent of the window. 
(3)  Wall signs . Wall signs are not permitted. 
(4)  Monument signs in subdivisions. Subdivision monument signs shall be governed by general subdivision entrance sign standards as provided in this division. 
(5)  Roof signs. Roof signs are not permitted. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2(A)) 
Sec. 26-868. - Single business lots in P-1, C-1, and C-2 zoning districts. 
For all uses other than residential planned developments in C-1 and C-2, the following signs are permitted on single business lots in P-1, C-1 and C-2 zoning districts: 
(1)  Ground signs. The permitted ground sign shall be limited to a maximum height of 30 feet above ground level, a maximum width of 25 feet, and maximum size as follows: 
a.  For lots containing a principal building of up to 10,000 square feet, one double-face sign per total road frontage with a maximum size of 112 square feet per face; 
b.  For lots containing a principal building of 10,001 to 100,000 square feet, one double-face sign per total road frontage with a maximum size of 150 square feet; and 
c.  For lots containing a principal building of 100,000 square feet or greater, one double-face sign per total road frontage with a maximum size of 200 square feet. 
(2)  Alternative ground signs. As an alternative to the ground sign permitted in subsection (1) of this section, one double-face monument sign is permitted, not to exceed 32 square feet per feet, with a maximum height of eight feet above ground level and a maximum width of 16 feet. 
(3)  Window signs. Total window signage for each exterior building wall may not exceed 25 percent of the area of all windows on that wall. 
(4)  Wall signs . Wall signs are limited to a total area of up to 100 square feet for all walls of business buildings up to 15,000 square feet and up to 200 square feet for all walls of business buildings of greater than 15,000 square feet. Wall signs may not exceed the height of the wall upon which they are attached or extend below the ceiling of any incorporated exterior walkway or other ceiling. 
(5)  Roof signs. Roof signs are not permitted. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2(B)) 
Sec. 26-869. - I-1 zoning districts. 
For all uses other than residential planned developments located in I-1 zoning districts, the following signs are permitted: 
(1)  Ground signs. The permitted ground sign shall be limited to a maximum height of 30 feet above ground level, a maximum width of 25 feet, and maximum size as follows: 
a.  For lots containing a principal building of up to 50,000 square feet, one double-face sign per total road frontage with a maximum size of 112 square feet per face; 
b.  For lots containing a principal building greater than 50,000 square feet, one double-face sign per total road frontage with a maximum size of 150 square feet. 
(2)  Alternative ground signs. As an alternative to the ground sign permitted in subsection (1) of this section, two double-face monument signs are permitted, placed one at each entrance, not to exceed 32 square feet per feet, with a maximum height of eight feet above ground level and a maximum width of 16 feet. 
(3)  Window signs. Total window signage may not exceed 25 percent of the total area of all windows facing road frontage. 
(4)  Wall signs . For industries having a principal building of up to 50,000 square feet, wall signs are limited to a total area of up to 100 square feet for all walls. For industries having a principal building of greater than 50,000 square feet, wall signs are limited to a total area of up to 200 square feet for all walls. Wall signs may not exceed the height of the wall to which they are attached or extend below the ceiling of any incorporated exterior walkway or other ceiling. 
(5)  Roof signs. Roof signs are not permitted. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2(C)) 
Sec. 26-870. - Residential planned development signs in C-1, C-2 and I-1 zoning districts. 
For residential planned developments located in C-1, C-2 and I-1 zoning districts, the following signs are permitted: 
(1)  Ground signs. The permitted ground sign shall be limited to a maximum height of 35 feet above ground level, a maximum width of 25 feet, and maximum size as follows: 
a.  For developments containing up to 50,000 total square feet, one double-face sign per total road frontage with a maximum size of 112 square feet per face, generally for purposes of presenting the development name; and 
b.  For developments containing greater than 50,000 total square feet, one double-face sign per total road frontage with a maximum size of 150 square feet, generally for purposes of present the development name. 
(2)  Window signs. Total window signage per business per wall may not exceed 25 percent of the total area of each wall. 
(3)  Wall signs . Wall signs may not exceed the height of the wall to which they are attached or extend below any incorporated exterior walkway or other ceiling. The maximum permitted size of wall signs shall be as follows: 
a.  Each individual commercial business having less than 15,000 square feet of gross floor area may erect up to two wall signs not to exceed a total of 100 square feet of sign space for all walls of each business. 
b.  Each individual commercial business having 15,000 square feet or more of gross floor area may erect up to four wall signs not to exceed a total of 200 square feet of sign space for all walls of each business. 
(4)  Roof signs. Roof signs are not permitted. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2(D)) 
Sec. 26-871. - Corner lot signs. 
Notwithstanding any other provisions of this article, single business and planned developments on corner lots are allowed ground signs on both roads or streets provided that the lot frontage on the secondary road, as designated by the state department of community affairs, must be a minimum of 200 feet. Corner lots have frontage on secondary roads of less than 200 feet shall be permitted one double-faced monument sign not to exceed 32 square feet of total area per sign face. Such signage limitations apply to each side of the lot having road or street frontage and shall not be accumulated and used on only one of the street frontages. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(J)) 
Sec. 26-872. - Subdivision entrance signs. 
One single- or double-face monument sign is permitted at every main entrance to any residential subdivision, mobile home park, mobile home subdivision, apartment complex, or other similar residential development. Such signs shall not exceed six feet in height, 12 feet in width, or 32 square feet of sign area for each face. Only external illumination is permitted. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(B)) 
Sec. 26-873. - Entrance and exit signs in commercial and industrial zones. 
In the commercial and industrial zones two single- or double-faced pole or monument-style signs each clearly indicating "Entrance" and "Exit" respectively are permitted. Each sign may not exceed three feet in height or three square feet of total area per sign face. Such signs shall be internally illuminated only and shall be placed at least five feet back from the road right-of-way. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(C)) 
Sec. 26-874. - Public purpose and safety signs. 
State and local public purpose and safety signs are permitted in every zoning district. Such signs can be placed in the right-of-way provided that they do not create a safety hazard. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(D)) 
Sec. 26-875. - Real estate signs. 
One non-animated real estate sign, per agency, per lot is permitted. Such signs shall not require a permit and shall be limited to signs whose permitted maximum display surface area does not exceed four square feet in residential district and 16 square feet in commercial districts. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(G)) 
Sec. 26-876. - Construction and improvement signs. 
(a)  Residential home construction and improvement signs may be placed on the site of the construction or repair, provided all such signs do not exceed six square feet in size and are removed within seven days after completion of work. 
(b)  Commercial and industrial construction signs displaying the intended occupant (i.e. "Coming Soon") or the names of the contractors or subcontractors may be placed on the site of the construction or repair, provided all such signs do not exceed 32 square feet and are removed within seven days after cessation or completion of construction. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(H)) 
Sec. 26-877. - Political signs. 
Political signs shall require no permit and may be permitted in all zoning districts. Such signs shall be limited to one single-face sign per road frontage and shall not exceed six square feet of total sign face area in any residential zoning district or 32 square feet of total sign face area in nonresidential zoning districts. Signs shall be permitted to be display eight weeks prior to the election and must be removed within 14 days following any election or runoff election and shall thereafter be forfeited to the city for immediate removal. All such signs shall conform to any other applicable provisions of these regulations. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(K)) 
Sec. 26-878. - Strip panel rotating signs. 
Strip panel rotating sign faces shall be permitted; however, such rotation is restricted to the vertical strip sign advertising face only where such strips do not exceed six inches in width. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(L)) 
Sec. 26-879. - Double-face copy change board signs. 
In addition to any single-support sign permitted in the C and M zoning districts, a double-faced copy change board may also be permitted in those same districts, excluding any planned developments. Such sign shall be located on the same support structure, separate from and below the main sign, and may not exceed four feet by eight feet. Double-face copy-change board signs may not be placed lower than ten feet above common grade level. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(M)) 
Sec. 26-880. - Individual vehicles signs. 
Vehicles may display up to four square feet of signage. Such signs shall be attached or be adhered directly to the body of the vehicle. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(A)) 
Sec. 26-881. - Holiday lighting. 
Holiday lights and decorations with no commercial message, illuminated only between November 1 and January 15, are permitted in all districts. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-2-2(F)) 
Secs. 26-882—26-910. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - PROHIBITED SIGNS 

Sec. 26-911. - Designated. 
Signs that are prohibited include, but are not limited to: 
(1)  Roof signs. 
(2)  Sidewalk, A-frame, sandwich type, curb type, or daily placement signs. 
(3)  Portable signs, except as otherwise specifically provided in this article. 
(4)  Animated signs involving motion or sound, including rotating signs or parts thereof. 
(5)  Flashing, blinking, or signs of varying light intensity with the exception of signs giving the time and temperature. 
(6)  Exposed neon or signs containing exposed neon tubing which are not enclosed within a channel or box lettering. 
(7)  Lighter than air, balloon, blimp, or other inflatable device which is tethered. 
(8)  Signs that contain or are an imitation of an official traffic sign or signal, or can be confused with an official traffic sign including those signs employing the word "Stop", "Yield", "Go", etc. 
(9)  Signs that have been abandoned, including signs that advertise an activity, business, product or service no longer active or in existence. 
(10)  Banners within 20 feet of a property line or right-of-way. 
(11)  Signs not in good repair, specifically including any sign which is in a state of disrepair or disassembly, or any sign which has its internal lighting exposed to view for more than one week. 
(12)  Signs or advertising devices attached directly onto any vehicle parked for more than 48 hours so as to be visible from a public right-of-way, except for work vehicles of a business and common carriers or other vehicles used for daily transportation. 
(13)  Canopies or awnings having a commercial message sign attached to or incorporated within the canopy or awning, with the exception of the name and address of the establishment. 
(14)  Streamers or beacons. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 19-3(A)—(N)) 
Sec. 26-912. - Forfeiture of signs; costs of removal. 
(a)  The following signs may be forfeited to the public and are subject to immediate confiscation by the city: 
(1)  Any sign installed or placed on public property, including right-of-ways, except in conformance with the requirements of this article; 
(2)  Any sign attached to any street sign or marker, traffic control signs or devices; 
(3)  Any sign attached to or painted on any sign pole or any post, tree, rock, or other natural object or feature. 
(b)  In addition to all other remedies available to the city under this Code or state law, the city shall have the right to recover from the sign owner or persons placing or maintaining signs enumerated in subsection (a) of this section the full costs of removal and disposal of such sign. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-3(O)) 
Secs. 26-913—26-942. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - TEMPORARY SIGNS 

Sec. 26-943. - Short duration signs (1—14 days). 
(a)  Generally. Except as otherwise specifically provided in this section for weekend signs: 
(1)  Short duration temporary signs can be erected in any zoning district for a maximum of two weeks. No more than two signs can be erected on any lot at one time. 
(2)  Such signs shall not exceed six feet in height and 16 square feet per side, and shall not be more than two-sided. 
(3)  Such signs shall be made of waterproof material, and must be attached to an independent mounting device. The mounting must be secure to prevent the sign from being blown off the device. (See subsection (b)(2) of this section.) The mounting device or sign should bear the name and phone number of the party responsible for the device. 
(4)  No such sign can be placed within 100 feet of an intersection or closer than ten feet from the pavement of the roadway. In no event shall such signs be placed on a public right-of-way. 
(5)  Short duration signs cannot be placed on the same lot more than four times per year. 
(b)  Weekend signs. 
(1)  Weekend signs shall not exceed three feet in height and four square feet per side, and shall not be more than two-sided. 
(2)  Such signs shall be made of waterproof material, and must be attached to an independent mounting device no more than 40 inches above ground level. The mounting must be secure to prevent the sign from being blown off the device. The sign or mounting device should bear the name and phone number of the party responsible for the device. 
(3)  No such sign can be placed within 100 feet of an intersection, nor shall any sign be closer than ten feet to the pavement of a roadway. In no event can such signs be placed on a public right-of-way. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-5.2(b)) 
Sec. 26-944. - Long duration signs (15—60 days). 
(a)  A temporary permit may be issued for long duration temporary signs permitted pursuant to this section. Such permits shall not be issued for signs intended to be used for less than 15 days and shall be valid for not more than 60 days. A business or individual cannot request more than one temporary permit for long duration signs every six months. 
(b)  Only one long duration temporary sign or device may be used on one lot at the same time. 
(c)  The types of long duration temporary signs that may be displayed only in the C and I zoning districts upon the issuance of a temporary permit for a long duration temporary sign by the zoning board are: 
(1)  Inflatable ground advertising devices and figures; 
(2)  Search lights, lasers and similar devices; and 
(3)  Banners, including flag banners. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-5.1) 
Secs. 26-945—26-961. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - DESIGN STANDARDS AND SPECIFICATIONS 

Sec. 26-962. - Applicability. 
The standards and specifications of this division shall apply to all signs in the city notwithstanding any other provision of this article. 
Sec. 26-963. - Construction and maintenance. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful to erect or place any sign which does not conform to the requirements of this article. 
(b)  All signs for which a permit is required, together with all their supports, shall be kept in constant repair and, unless constructed of galvanized or noncorroding metal, shall periodically be given a protective coating. The area immediately in front of all freestanding signs shall be maintained free of high weeds and debris. 
(c)  The staff of the zoning board may periodically inspect every sign in order to determine that each meets the requirements set forth in this article. 
(d)  The owner or entity shall be required to remove or have removed from the premises discarded or unusable paper, sign faces, parts and debris resulting from the changing of the advertising copy or message or maintenance of any sign or sign structure. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9) 
Sec. 26-964. - Computation of total sign area. 
The area of a sign shall be computed as the area within the smallest square, rectangle, or portion thereof enclosing, or which would have enclosed, the outer limits of the sign face and frame, text, material, texture, or color forming an integral part of the sign or used to differentiate the sign face and frame from the structure upon which it is placed. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(A)) 
Sec. 26-965. - Content. 
Any sign, display or device allowed under this chapter may contain any commercial or noncommercial message, except that such messages cannot be profane, depict obscenity as defined by O.C.G.A. § 16-12-80, depict sexual conduct or sexually explicit nudity as defined by O.C.G.A. § 36-60-3, or advertise any illegal activity. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(B)) 
Sec. 26-966. - Embellishments. 
Sign embellishments (including protrusions) shall not constitute greater than 20 percent of the surface of the sign face or perimeter. Protrusions greater than 12 inches from the sign face and 18 inches from the sign perimeter are prohibited. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(C)) 
Sec. 26-967. - Number. 
For the purposes of determining the number of signs, ground signs shall be equal to the number of sign structures. All other (non-ground signs shall be considered to be a single display surface or display device containing elements organized, related and composed to form a unit. Where matter is displayed in random manner without organized relationship of elements, such elements shall be considered to be a single sign. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(D)) 
Sec. 26-968. - Illumination. 
(a)  Ground signs shall not be internally illuminated in the residential districts (D-1, R-1, R-2, RMH). All external lighting shall be positioned and shielded so that the light source cannot be seen directly by any passing motorist or cause detriment to any surrounding businesses for residents. 
(b)  Flashing, blinking or other illumination of varying degree is not permitted. Lighting that causes confusion with, or distraction from, any traffic signal or safety device shall not be permitted. 
(c)  All externally illuminated signs shall utilize low wattage luminaries mounted in fixtures designed to direct the light and eliminate light trespass. 
(d)  All internally illuminated signs shall utilize low wattage luminaries designed to reduce light glow. 
(e)  All signs over six feet in height shall be internally illuminated or by external lighting fixtures located below the sign area. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(E)) 
Sec. 26-969. - Support and stabilization. 
With the exception of planned development signs that may be of a double-pole type, all other signs, banners, and the like shall be self-supporting upon a single support (e.g., a monopole) and within its own framework structure. Such signs shall not employ the use of guy wires or other external support bracing for stabilization. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(F)) 
Sec. 26-970. - Setbacks. 
All signs or protrusions thereof that are located on the ground must be setback at least five feet from any public right-of-way or property line. No permanently affixed ground sign shall interfere with any public utility or vehicular line of sight. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(G)) 
Sec. 26-971. - Corner visibility. 
No sign or sign structure above the height of three feet may be sited within 15 feet of the intersection of the right-of-way lines of either street. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(H)) 
Sec. 26-972. - Fire safety restrictions. 
No sign or sign structure may be erected or maintained which obstructs any form of fire escape or fire lane. No sign or portion of a sign may project or extend over any residential, commercial, industrial structure, any driveway, walkway or the like. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-4(I)) 
Secs. 26-973—26-1002. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - NONCONFORMING SIGNS 

Sec. 26-1003. - What constitutes; when removal required. 
(a)  Signs that do not comply with this article and that were legally placed before the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived shall be nonconforming with respect to the requirements of this article and subject to the provisions of this division. Signs that were illegally erected, established or maintained with respect to the applicable requirements of prior city sign regulations are not nonconforming signs under this division and shall be removed or brought into compliance with this article. 
(b)  Nonconforming signs made of paper, cloth or other non-durable material, all temporary signs other than those permitted in this article, and any signs that are not affixed to a building or the ground or are located within a public right-of-way, must be removed by the sign or property owner. 
(c)  Upon failure to comply with the requirements of this article, the zoning board may cause the removal of any nonconforming sign at the expense of the owner or associated party. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9(1)) 
Sec. 26-1004. - Replacement. 
(a)  A nonconforming sign shall not be replaced by another nonconforming sign except that the substitution or interchange of advertising panels, painted boards or demountable material on nonconforming signs shall be permitted. 
(b)  Those signs considered nonconforming (grandfathered) as of December 1, 2003, shall be governed by the signage requirements for the zoning classification, as designated by the department of community affairs, that most closely approximates its use. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9(2)) 
Sec. 26-1005. - Repair and maintenance. 
Minor repairs and maintenance of nonconforming signs such as repainting, electrical repairs and neon tubing may be permitted. However, no structural repairs or changes in the size or shape of the sign shall be permitted except to make the sign comply with the requirements of this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9(3)) 
Sec. 26-1006. - Relocation if removal necessitated by city or state improvement projects. 
If a nonconforming sign must be removed due to a city or state road improvement or other project, the zoning board may authorize the relocation of such sign even though the new location may not meet the setback requirements or other provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9(4)) 
Secs. 26-1007—26-1025. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 7. - SIGN PERMITS 

Sec. 26-1026. - Required; exceptions. 
(a)  A sign permit is not required for the erection of a weekend sign, or a ground or window sign in the D-1, R-1, R-2, RMH zoning districts; provided, however, that the exception provided in this subsection shall not act to exempt signs using electrical wiring and connections from the requirement for electrical permitting. 
(b)  For all other signs, a sign permit is required before a ground or wall sign may be erected and before an existing sign may be enlarged, relocated, or materially improved upon to an extent of 60 percent of its total replacement value. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.1(a)) 
Sec. 26-1027. - Issuance subject to applicability and conformance. 
A sign permit shall be issued by the building official when the plans, specifications, and intended use of the applied sign or part thereof conform to the applicable provisions of this chapter. The application shall be accompanied by all the information required under this division and such other information as the building official may require. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.1(b)) 
Sec. 26-1028. - Applications; time for processing; grounds for denial. 
(a)  Applications for sign permits shall be filed by the sign owner or owner's agent with the building official upon forms as provided. Any information pertinent to the sign application as may be requested by the zoning board and may include, but not limited to: 
(1)  The type and purpose of the sign as defined by this article or the state department of community affairs (DCA). 
(2)  A site plan showing the location of the sign, and construction plan describing the material the sign is to be constructed from. 
(3)  Elevation drawing showing the height and dimensions of the sign face. 
(4)  The total construction cost of the sign. 
(5)  The street address of the property upon which the subject sign is to be located and the proposed location of the sign on the subject property. In the absence of a street address, a method of location acceptable to the department of community affairs shall be used. 
(6)  The square foot area per sign face and the aggregate square foot area if there is more than one sign face. 
(7)  The names and addresses of the owners of the real property upon which the subject sign is to be located. 
(8)  The name, address, phone number, and business license number and home jurisdiction of the sign contractor. 
(b)  Upon receipt of an application for a sign as permitted under the provisions of this section, the zoning board, shall examine and process the application within 15 working days. 
(c)  A permit may be denied if the applicant, landowner, or lessee or other party is presently maintaining any sign in violation of the sign provision of this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 19-6.2, 19-6.4) 
Sec. 26-1029. - Indemnification and hold harmless agreement and liability insurance required. 
Each sign application shall contain an agreement to indemnify and hold the city harmless of all damages, demands, or expenses which may in any manner be caused by the sign, or the sign's erection, continued existence, or removal. Each applicant shall present to the city upon request a certificate of liability insurance prior to the issuance of a sign permit. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 19-6.1(c), 19-6.4) 
Sec. 26-1030. - Expiration date. 
A sign permit shall become null and void if the sign for which the permit was issued has not been completed within six months after the date of issuance; provided, however, that a six month extension of the permit may be granted by the building official. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.3) 
Sec. 26-1031. - Fees. 
No permit should be issued until the appropriate application has been filed with the zoning board and the appropriate fee has been paid, which fees shall from time to time be established by the city council. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.5) 
Sec. 26-1032. - Electrical permits required. 
All signs in the city using electrical wiring and connection shall require an electrical permit regardless of whether a sign permit is required under the provisions of this article. 
Sec. 26-1033. - Appeal of permit denial. 
Upon denial of an application for a sign permit, the applicant shall be given verbal notice or written notice within 15 days of the denial stating the reasons for denial of the permit. The aggrieved party may appeal any decision as provided in the manner as provided in this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.7) 
Sec. 26-1034. - Variances. 
(a)  By zoning administrator. Administrative variances to the requirements of this article may be granted by the zoning administrator, provided that any variance that is granted should conform to the intent and purpose of this article. 
(b)  By city council. Variances may be granted from the provision of this chapter by the city council as recommended by the zoning board and shall apply both to signs that are nonconforming as of the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived as well as the new signs erected thereafter. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.8) 
Secs. 26-1035—26-1051. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 8. - ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 26-1052. - Right of entry for inspection. 
City enforcement personnel are hereby empowered to enter upon or into a building, structure, or premises upon which a sign is located for the purpose of inspecting the sign, or its structural and electrical connections, and to ensure compliance with the provision of this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.6) 
Sec. 26-1053. - Removal after notice. 
(a)  Authority. City enforcement personnel may order the removal of any sign in violation of this article. 
(b)  Notice required. Except as otherwise specifically provided in this division, notice of noncompliance shall be given to the permit holder or property owner, then to the owner of the sign, or, if the sign owner cannot be found or cannot be determined, notice shall be given to the sign erector or property owner, or any party associated with such sign. 
(c)  Grounds for order of removal generally. Except as otherwise provided herein with regard to invalid sign permits, the removal order shall be issued only after the appropriate party fails to comply with the terms of this article for seven working days after the receipt of written notice of noncompliance from the zoning board or other authorized enforcement personnel or within ten working days from the mailing of such notice, if no return receipt is received indicating acceptance. 
(d)  Removal resulting from invalid permit. City enforcement personnel may issue a removal order when it has been determined: 
(1)  That a permit was improperly issued as a result of misstatement of fact or fraud; 
(2)  That the sign has not been placed or constructed in compliance with the specifications of the application or site plans; 
(3)  That the sign permit has expired; or 
(4)  That the sign is otherwise not in compliance with the article. 
(e)  Automatic revocation of sign permit. If a permit was issued, a notice given under this division shall operate to revoke the permit. 
(f)  Appeal. An aggrieved party may appeal the removal order within ten working days from the date that the notice was received in the same manner as provided in this chapter for permit denials. 
(g)  Effect of failure to remove; removal by city; costs. If the sign is not removed within 30 days after the order of removal is delivered or mailed, or 45 days from the mailing of such notice if no return receipt is received indicating acceptance, or 30 days after the date any appeal becomes final, city enforcement personnel are authorized to remove the sign or cause this sign to be removed and to collect the costs thereof as provided in this division. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9) 
Sec. 26-1054. - Removal without notice. 
City enforcement personnel or any other authorized city agent may remove or direct the removal of any sign in violation of this article without giving notice to any party, if the sign is on the public right-of-way or other public property or the sign poses an immediate safety threat to the life or health of any member of the public. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9) 
Sec. 26-1055. - Cost of removal. 
(a)  The removal or the cost of removal of any sign removed or ordered to be removed under this division shall be the responsibility of the sign owner without liability to the city, its officers, agents, servants and employees. 
(b)  If the sign owner cannot be found or cannot be determined, then the costs of removal shall be the joint and several responsibility of the sign erector or property owner or any other party associated with the placement of the sign. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9) 
Sec. 26-1056. - Collection of unpaid costs. 
If the sign is removed by the city and if payment is, or satisfactory arrangements to make payment are, not made by the property owner, sign erector, or owner within 30 days after the receipt of a statement for the costs of removal, city enforcement personnel shall certify the amount thereof for collection to the city attorney. The city shall be afforded all means available to remedy the collection of the reimbursable funds. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9) 
Sec. 26-1057. - Disposition of unclaimed removed signs. 
In the event any signs that are removed remain unclaimed for more than 60 days from the date of removal, the signs may be disposed of in accordance with state law. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9) 
Sec. 26-1058. - Penalties. 
Without limitation, sign erectors or owners, property owners or associated parties may be cited for the violation of any provision of this article and thereupon shall be subject to penalties provided in section 1-13. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 19-6.9) 
Secs. 26-1059—26-1084. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 26-1085. - Building official. 
The building official shall have the power and duty to provide the following services related to this chapter: 
(1)  Administer and enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
(2)  Issue and when necessary revoke building permits according to the procedures outlined in chapter. 
(3)  Issue a certificate of occupancy according to the procedures outlined in this chapter. 
(4)  Issue a sign permit when the applicant meets the requirements outlined in this chapter. 
(5)  Enter upon any premises for the purpose of making inspections of premises or buildings necessary to carry out his duties in the enforcement of this chapter. 
(6)  Maintain complete records concerning this chapter and related matter and make such records available to the public upon request. 
(7)  Maintain the official zoning map for public display. 
(8)  Advise the general public on how to comply with the requirements of this chapter. 
(9)  Maintain complete records concerning this chapter and related matter and make such records available to the public upon request. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-3) 
Sec. 26-1086. - Matter to be determined by the city council. 
The city council shall hear and make decisions concerning: 
(1)  Proposed amendments to this chapter. 
(2)  Adoption and amendment to the zoning map, including amendment of text. 
(3)  Approval, disapproval or other action on all requests for zoning changes as provided in this chapter. 
(4)  Upon consideration of the recommendation from the zoning board, grant or deny applications for variances from the requirements of this chapter. 
(5)  Approval or disapproval of conditional use permits. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-2) 
Sec. 26-1087. - Required disclosures. 
(a)  The provisions of O.C.G.A. § 45-10-1 et seq. require disclosure of financial interests by all government officials, including city council members and zoning board members, who will consider a rezoning action. State law also requires disclosure of campaign contributions or gifts by the rezoning applicant or his attorney. 
(b)  All government officials, including city councilmembers and zoning board members, are required to disclose in writing any ownership interest they have or any family members have, in real property made the subject of a rezoning request. Additionally, these officials are required to disclose in writing any financial interest of ten percent or more in any business entity which has an ownership interest in the property to be considered. 
(c)  An applicant for a rezoning and his attorney must disclose all campaign contributions or gifts aggregating $250.00 or more which were made within two years of the filing of the application for rezoning. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 1-5) 
State Law reference— Disclosure required to be in writing, O.C.G.A. § 36-67A-2. 
Sec. 26-1088. - Fees. 
Reasonable fees sufficient to cover the cost of administration, inspection, publication of notice and similar matters may be charged to applicants for rezoning applications, amendments to the map or text), variance applications, an appeal from action of the building official and other administrative relief. The amount of the fees charged shall be as set forth by the city. Fees shall be paid upon submission of a signed application or notice of appeal. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 21-8) 
Sec. 26-1089. - Remedies. 
If any building is erected, constructed, reconstructed, altered, repaired, converted or maintained, or any building or land is used in violation of this chapter, the building official or any other appropriate authority or any adjacent or neighboring property owner who would be damaged by such violation, in addition to other remedies, may institute injunction, mandamus or other appropriate action in proceeding to prevent such violation. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 21-10) 
Sec. 26-1090. - Penalties. 
(a)  Any person found in violation of any provision of the chapter shall be subject to a fine of not more than $500.00 per violation or imprisoned in the city jail for not more than 60 days, or both, and in addition shall pay the cost of such action. Each offense shall constitute a separate offense for each day such violation continues. 
(b)  The city, through its attorney or other official designated by the city council may, in addition to other remedies, institute injunction mandamus or other appropriate action or proceeding to enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
(c)  Any building erected in violation of this chapter shall be deemed an unlawful structure, and the building official, city attorney, or other official designated by the city council may bring appropriate action to enjoin such erection or cause it to be vacated or removed. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 21-9) 
Sec. 26-1091. - Judicial review. 
(a)  Any person or persons severally or jointly aggrieved by any decision of the zoning board or the mayor and city council relating to the regulations set forth in this chapter or with any official charged with the enforcement of any order, requirement or decision of said city council, any time may take an appeal to the county superior court in the manner provided by state law. 
(b)  If appeal is not filed in the manner and within the time provided by state law, the decision of the zoning board or the city council, or any official charged with the enforcement of any order, requirement or decision in connection therewith, shall be final. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 21-11) 
Secs. 26-1092—26-1120. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ZONING BOARD 

Sec. 26-1121. - Established. 
The zoning board is hereby established to hear and decide appeals and to recommend action to the mayor and city council for variances from the terms of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1, 3-1.1(a)) 
Sec. 26-1122. - Members; qualifications; terms. 
There shall be a zoning board consisting of six members appointed by the mayor and city council. Members appointed to the zoning board shall hold no other public office. All members shall be qualified electors of the city. Members shall serve overlapping terms of four years, except for the initial appointment in which three members shall be appointed for initial terms of four years and three members shall be appointed for three-year terms of office. Zoning board members may be appointed to succeed themselves and for terms of four years. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-1.1(b)) 
Sec. 26-1123. - Vacancies in office. 
Vacancies shall be filled for unexpired terms. A vacancy in a term of office shall occur whenever the mayor and city council finds that a member has resigned, or when the mayor and city council shall have dismissed a member because of his repeated failure to attend meetings of the zoning board without just cause, or because the member has been guilty of malfeasance or misconduct in office. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-1.1(c)) 
Sec. 26-1124. - Organization. 
The zoning board shall hold an annual organizational meeting and shall elect a chairperson and vice-chairperson from among its members before proceeding to any other matters of business. Newly appointed members shall be installed at the first regular meeting after their appointment. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-1.1(d)) 
Sec. 26-1125. - Rules of procedure. 
The zoning board may adopt its own rules of procedure and keep a record of its proceedings in accordance with the state statutes and these regulations. 
Sec. 26-1126. - Meetings. 
The zoning board shall meet at the call of the chairperson and shall designate the time and place of its meetings. The members of the zoning board shall regularly attend meetings and public hearings of the zoning board. Minutes shall be kept of all zoning board proceedings. All zoning board meetings shall be open to the public. Whenever feasible the agenda for each meeting shall be made available in advance of the meeting. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-1.2) 
Sec. 26-1127. - Quorum and voting. 
Four members of the zoning board shall constitute a quorum for the conduct of business. All actions of the zoning board shall be taken by a majority vote, a quorum being present. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-1.3; Ord. of 3-2011) 
Sec. 26-1128. - Powers and duties. 
The zoning board does not have the power to amend any zoning ordinance regulations, to rezone any land, to declare this chapter or any amendment thereto invalid or to allow any use not permitted by this chapter. The zoning board does have the power and duty to: 
(1)  Recommend to the mayor and city council changes in the zoning ordinance that the zoning board believes are appropriate. 
(2)  Recommend to the mayor and city council approval, disapproval or other action on all requests for zoning changes as provided in this chapter. 
(3)  Hear requests for the interpretation of the official zoning map and for any special questions upon which the zoning board is authorized to pass. 
(4)  To hear and decide appeals where it is alleged by the appellant that there is error in any order, requirement, permit, decision, determination or refusal made by the building official or other administrative official in the carrying out or enforcement of any provision of this chapter, as provided in this chapter. 
(5)  The zoning board shall hear and recommend to the mayor and city council applications for variances from the requirements of this chapter, as provided in this chapter. 
(6)  Conduct such other business and affairs as may be, from time to time, designated by the mayor and city council. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-1.4(a)—(d)) 
Sec. 26-1129. - Appeal of zoning board action. 
Any person or persons, jointly or separately, aggrieved by any decision of the zoning board may appeal to the county superior court in the manner provided by state law. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 22-5) 
Secs. 26-1130—26-1151. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - APPEALS, VARIANCES, AND CONDITIONAL USES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 26-1152. - Application forms; fees; time for filing. 
Applications for hearing and decision on requests for an appeal, a variance, or a conditional use shall be submitted to the building official on forms approved by the city council, together with a fee in the amount determined by the city council, at least 30 days prior to the next regularly schedule meeting of the zoning board. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.5, 22-4(a)) 
Sec. 26-1153. - Contents of application. 
Each application shall contain such information as the building official may require to enable the zoning board to make its decision on an appeal or conditional use, or a recommendation on a variance request. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.5, 22-4(a)) 
Sec. 26-1154. - Time for scheduling public hearing. 
Within a reasonable time after receiving an application for an appeal, variance, or conditional use, the zoning board shall schedule a public hearing. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.5, 22-4) 
Sec. 26-1155. - Notices of hearing. 
(a)  The zoning board shall publish once in a newspaper of general circulation in the city a written notice of such public hearing at least 15 days but not more than 45 days prior to the public hearing. The public notice shall indicate the time, place and nature of the appeal, variance or conditional use to be considered by the zoning board. 
(b)  Additionally, at least 15 days before the scheduled public hearing, the building official shall post, in a conspicuous place on the property that is the subject of the application, a sign at least two feet by three feet in size. The sign shall set forth the time, place and purpose of the public hearing before the zoning board. Acts of vandalism or natural occurrences limiting the effectiveness of notice by a sign posted on the property shall not invalidate any proceedings or action taken under this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.5(b), 22-4(b)) 
Sec. 26-1156. - Rights of parties to present evidence. 
The appellant and any public agency or private individual shall be entitled to present evidence on matters before the zoning board at the public hearing required by this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-14(e)(3), 22-1.3) 
Secs. 26-1157—26-1175. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - APPEALS 

Sec. 26-1176. - Actions subject to appeal. 
The zoning board shall hear and decide appeals where it is alleged by the appellant that there is an error in any order, requirement, permit, decision or refusal made by the building official or other administrative official in the administration or enforcement of any provisions of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(d), 22-1) 
Sec. 26-1177. - Persons who may seek appeal. 
An appeal to the zoning board may be taken by any person, firm or corporation aggrieved or by any governmental officer, department, board or agency affected by any decision of the building official or other administrative official with respect to this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3.14(e)(1), 22-1.1) 
Sec. 26-1178. - Notice of appeal; time for filing; transmittal to zoning board. 
Appeals under this article shall be made within 15 days following notification of the decision appealed from by filing with the zoning board a notice of appeal specifying the grounds thereof. The building official shall forthwith transmit to the zoning board all the papers constituting the record upon which the action was taken. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3.14(e)(1), 22-1.1) 
Sec. 26-1179. - Stay of proceedings. 
An appeal under this division stays all actions by the building official seeking enforcement of or compliance with the order or decision appealed from, unless the building official certifies to the zoning board that a stay would, in his opinion, cause imminent peril to life or property. In such case, proceedings shall not be stayed otherwise than by a restraining order which may be granted by a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-14(e)(2), 22-1.2) 
Sec. 26-1180. - Withdrawal of appeal. 
Any appeal may be withdrawn upon written notice to the city clerk or building official and city clerk, but no appeal shall be withdrawn after the posting of a hearing notice or prior to the zoning board's action thereon without formal consent of the zoning board. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-14(e)(4)) 
Sec. 26-1181. - Determinations by zoning board. 
The zoning board may modify in whole or in part any order, requirement, or decision of the building official and, to that end, shall have the power of the building official or administrative official from whom the appeal is taken. The zoning board may direct the issuance of a permit. It shall be the duty of the building official to carry out the decisions of the zoning board. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(e)(5), 22-1.4) 
Secs. 26-1182—26-1210. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - VARIANCES 

Sec. 26-1211. - Types of matter subject to application for variance. 
(a)  The zoning board shall hear and recommend to the mayor and city council applications for variances from the requirements of this chapter, but only in individual cases of practical difficulty or unnecessary hardship. Such cases may include: 
(1)  Exceptional narrowness, shallowness or shape of a specific piece of property that at the time of adoption of this chapter was a lot or plat of record; or 
(2)  When by reason of exceptional topographic conditions or other extraordinary or exceptional conditions of a piece of property, the strict application of the requirements of this chapter would result in practical difficulties to, or undue hardship upon, the owner of such property. 
(b)  The zoning board shall not be authorized to recommend a density variance or a use variance to permit a use in a district in which the use is prohibited. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(f), 22-3) 
Sec. 26-1212. - Applications. 
In addition to any other information required generally for applications under this chapter, each application for a variance shall include a plat drawn to scale showing the following information: 
(1)  All property lines, with dimensions. 
(2)  Location of buildings and other structures, creeks and easements referenced to the property line of the property in question. 
(3)  The north arrow, land district and land lot marker. 
(4)  Location of setback lines or other dimensional requirements from which the variance is sought. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 3-1.5(a)) 
Sec. 26-1213. - Time within which determination on application must be made. 
The zoning board shall consider and decide whether to recommend approval or disapproval of a variance request within 45 days after the public hearing thereon. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 22-3.4) 
Sec. 26-1214. - Burden of proof. 
In reviewing an application for a variance, the burden of showing that the variance should be granted shall be upon the person applying therefor. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(f), 22-3) 
Sec. 26-1215. - Required findings for recommendation of variance. 
No variance shall be recommended unless the zoning board finds that all of the following conditions exist: 
(1)  There are extraordinary and exceptional conditions pertaining to the particular parcel of property in question because of its size, shape, or topography. 
(2)  The application of this chapter to this particular piece of property would create an unnecessary hardship. 
(3)  Such conditions are peculiar to the particular piece of property involved and do not apply generally to other land or buildings in the vicinity. 
(4)  Relief, if granted, would not cause substantial detriment to the public good or impair the purposes and intent of this chapter; provided, however, that no variance may be granted for a use of land or building or structure that is prohibited in a given district by this chapter. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(f), 22-3) 
Sec. 26-1216. - Conditional variances. 
During its review of a variance request, the zoning board may attach thereto such conditions regarding the location, character and other features of the proposed building, structure or use as it may deem advisable so that the purpose of this chapter will be served and to provide adequately for the maintenance of the integrity and character of the zone in which such permit is granted. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(f), 22-3.1) 
Sec. 26-1217. - Guarantees; violation of conditions. 
When necessary, the zoning board may require guarantees, in such form as it deems proper, to ensure that conditions designated in connection therewith are being or will be complied with. Where any condition under which a request has been granted appears to have been violated, the zoning board may hold a public hearing thereon to determine whether or not the permit theretofore granted shall be terminated. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(f), 22-3.2) 
Sec. 26-1218. - Subdivision regulation variances. 
The zoning board may recommend, and the mayor and city council may grant, variances from the required improvements and minimum standards of design contained in the city's subdivision regulations; provided that the subdivider makes a specific request and shows to the satisfaction of the zoning board and the mayor and city council that topographical or other conditions peculiar and particular to the site are such that strict adherence to the requirements would cause him unnecessary hardship and would not carry out the intent of these regulations. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 22-3.3) 
Sec. 26-1219. - Effective time period. 
The zoning board, upon recommendation, and subsequently, the mayor and city council, when granting a variance, may establish a time period for said variance. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(f), 22-3.5) 
Sec. 26-1220. - Grant to be included in minutes. 
The grant of a variance shall be stated in the minutes with the reasons for departure from the strict application of this chapter and the conditions under which the variance was granted. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(f), 22-3.5) 
Sec. 26-1221. - Termination. 
Any variance granted shall terminate automatically when the use ceases to be in full compliance with any conditions imposed by the zoning board, when the use has been abandoned, or when the building permit shall have expired. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, §§ 3-1.4(f), 22-3.5) 
Secs. 26-1222—26-1245. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - CONDITIONAL USES 

Sec. 26-1246. - Certain uses and conditions allowed. 
Some zoning districts permit certain uses only upon approval of the zoning board. These uses are identified in this chapter as conditional uses and such uses may be allowed under special conditions. The granting of a conditional use does not constitute a permanent change in zoning or use. The conditional use may be forfeited if it does not meet the criteria provided in this section. Generally, a conditional use shall be compatible with the applicable zoning district under special conditions. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 22-2) 
Sec. 26-1247. - Approval. 
Conditional uses shall be permitted subject to an approval by the zoning in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. The required review shall determine whether the uses conform to the standards set forth in this article. 
Sec. 26-1248. - Conditions and development standards. 
(a)  The conditional use shall be approved if it meets all the following factors: 
(1)  A rezoning to a more intensive zoning district, which contains that use as a use by right, would not be appropriate for the property. 
(2)  The location and character of the conditional use shall be compatible with the community development pattern and consistent with the needs of the neighborhood. 
(3)  The conditional use will not be injurious to the use and enjoyment of the natural environment or of other property in the immediate vicinity, or diminish and impair property values within the surrounding neighborhood. 
(4)  The conditional use will not increase state or local expenditures in relation to the cost of servicing or maintaining neighborhood properties. 
(b)  The zoning board may impose any additional conditions and development standards, along with the grant of the conditional use, as may be necessary to protect the health, safety and welfare of surrounding landowners, neighborhoods and workers. The zoning board may require as part of its approval, the following conditions: 
(1)  Planted or screen buffers to reduce adverse or potentially adverse effects on adjoining properties. 
(2)  Limitation of street access ways, parking areas, and loading docks. 
(3)  The rearrangement of structures on the development site. 
(4)  Increases in maximum building height. 
(5)  Increases in the district requirements for lot size and building line setbacks, but not a reduction of these requirements. 
(6)  Limitations on the hours of business operation when it can be shown that proposed operational times would cause an adverse effect on adjoining, existing uses. 
(7)  Specified distances from existing residential, public, or institutional developments. 
(c)  In no case, however, shall the zoning board exempt any conditional use from meeting the minimum lot and structure requirements of the zoning district in which the proposed use is to be located. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 22-2(b), (c)) 
Secs. 26-1249—26-1269. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - AMENDMENTS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 26-1270. - Amendment defined. 
As used in this article, the term "amendment" shall mean both a change to the official zoning map and a change to the text of this chapter unless otherwise indicated. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-1(b)) 
Sec. 26-1271. - Grounds for amendment. 
The mayor and city council may from time to time, amend these regulations set forth in this chapter or the boundaries of the zoning districts established on the zoning map subject to the conditions provided in this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-1) 
Sec. 26-1272. - Purpose and intent. 
(a)  Generally. The exercise of the zoning power by the city, including the city's authority to amend this chapter, shall constitute an effort to balance the interest of the community in promoting the public health, safety, morality and general welfare against the right of property owners to the unrestricted use of their property. 
(b)  Compatibility of uses; preservation of value. Further, it is the policy and intent of the city to exercise the zoning power for purposes of assuring the compatibility of use of adjacent and nearby properties and the preservation of the economic value of adjacent and nearby properties while enabling a reasonable use of all property. 
(c)  Conformity to comprehensive plan. It is further the policy of the city to exercise its zoning power in conformity with the policy and intent of the city comprehensive plan insofar as that plan is current in its application to the specific property that is the subject of the proposed amendment. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-3) 
Sec. 26-1273. - Factors to be considered by zoning board and city council. 
(a)  The factors set forth in this section shall be considered by the zoning board when reviewing and making its written recommendation and by the city council when making a decision whether to approve or deny the requested amendment. These factors are determined to be relevant in balancing the interest in promoting the public health, safety, morality and general welfare against the right to the unrestricted use of the property. 
(b)  The relevant factors to be considered by the zoning board and the city council under this section are: 
(1)  Whether the proposed amendment would allow a use that is generally suitable for the site compared to other possible uses and the uses and zoning of adjacent and nearby properties; 
(2)  Whether the proposed amendment would adversely affect the economic value or the uses of adjacent and nearby properties; 
(3)  Whether the property to be affected by the proposed amendment can be used as currently zoned; 
(4)  Whether the proposed amendment, if adopted, would result in a use which would or could cause an excessive or burdensome use of existing streets, schools, sewers, water resources, police and fire protection or other utilities; and 
(5)  Whether there are other conditions or transitional patterns affecting the use and development of the property sought to be rezoned, if applicable, which give ground for either approval or disapproval of the proposed amendment. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-3) 
Secs. 26-1274—26-1304. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PROCEDURE 

Sec. 26-1305. - Persons who may initiate amendment proceedings. 
No amendment shall become effective unless it shall have been initiated by the city council, the zoning, board, the property owners, an individual who has the owners' power of attorney authorizing him to act, or a request signed by 60 percent of the property owners who hold not less than 60 percent of the affected land. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-1(a)) 
Sec. 26-1306. - Applications. 
Applications proposing amendments to the text of this chapter or to the city zoning map shall be submitted in writing to the city building official on a form providing by the city, together with a fee in the amount established by the city council. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-2(a)) 
Sec. 26-1307. - Applications regarding property in violation of chapter not accepted. 
(a)  No application will be accepted from any person regarding any property that is in violation of this chapter. 
(b)  If at the time of application the property that is the subject of an amendment or any other action of the mayor and city council is found to be in violation of this chapter, the building official will not accept or process any application from that applicant until the applicant voluntarily removes or changes the cause of the violation or ceases to be in violation. The applicant must then notify the building official that he is no longer in violation and obtain a release from the building official as to the violation. Once released, the mayor and city council will then accept the application for amendment of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-2(b)) 
Sec. 26-1308. - Review by zoning board; findings and recommendation. 
(a)  All proposed amendments shall be submitted to the building official, who shall then refer the proposals for amendment to the zoning board. It will study the proposed amendment and determine if it meets the standards provided in this chapter. 
(b)  The zoning board shall submit its findings and recommendations to the mayor and city council within 30 days from the date it received the petition. 
(c)  If the zoning board fails to submit a report within a 30-day period, it shall be deemed to have approved the requested change. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-2(c)) 
Sec. 26-1309. - Public notice. 
(a)  At least 15 but not more than 45 days prior to the scheduled public hearing, the building official shall file a notice of public hearing which shall be published in the newspaper of general circulation in the city setting forth the time, place, and purpose of the hearing. Such notice shall indicate the nature of the change proposed, identify the property affected. The cost of such newspaper notice shall be paid by the applicant for zoning amendment. 
(b)  When a proposed amendment affects the district classification of particular parcels of property, the building official shall place conspicuously on the property that is the subject of the amendment, not less than 15 days prior to the public hearing, a sign not less than nine feet square, with not less than three-inch black letters upon a white background. The notice to be included in the sign shall be in the form prescribed from time to time by the city council. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-5) 
Sec. 26-1310. - Public hearing. 
(a)  Required. Before taking action on a proposed amendment, the mayor and city council shall hold a public hearing thereon. 
(b)  Time and place. A public hearing shall be conducted at the time and place specified by the mayor and city council and as set forth in the public notice thereof. 
(c)  Purpose. The purpose of such hearing shall be to present to the public the proposed zoning amendment, and to receive comments thereon from the public. The mayor and city council shall consider the proceedings and comments of such hearing on the proposed zoning amendment in making a final decision on whether to approve or deny the amendment application. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-4) 
Sec. 26-1311. - Conduct of hearings. 
(a)  The hearing shall be convened by the mayor at the time and place scheduled. 
(b)  The mayor shall open any hearing with an explanation of the purpose of the hearing and a description of the general rules for the conduct of the hearing. The mayor or his delegate may describe the authority and role of the city council in any zoning decision. 
(c)  The mayor shall review the procedures for holding the public hearing which shall be as follows: 
(1)  No person may speak until recognized by the mayor. Upon rising to speak, the person recognized must first state his name and address. 
(2)  The person speaking will be allowed two minutes to express opinions and make points on each separate element of the proposed zoning revisions which he wishes to address; provided, however, that no person shall speak longer than an aggregate of ten minutes. 
(3)  The mayor or his delegate shall allow the person initiating the proposed zoning amendment or his designee to present a description of the proposed zoning amendment and the reasons for initiating the proposed zoning amendment. 
(4)  The mayor or his delegate shall give persons opposed to the proposed amendment the opportunity to address the city council. 
(5)  Any remark amounting to attack on the character or personal integrity of another individual, or comment not factually supportable, or comment in the form of an emotional outburst, shall be non-germane to the purpose of any hearing and may be ruled out of order. 
(6)  Additional persons will be recognized in accordance with the procedure set forth above for the purpose of addressing additional issues and making additional points, but no speaker shall be allowed to address points which have already been thoroughly discussed. 
(7)  Upon conclusion of the presentation of persons opposing the proposed zoning amendment, the mayor or his delegate shall afford the person initiating the petition an allotted time to address the mayor and city council in rebuttal of any issues raised by persons addressing the city council in opposition to the proposed zoning amendment. 
(d)  When proponents and opponents of the proposed zoning amendment have been heard in accordance with the foregoing procedures, the mayor or his delegate shall declare the public hearing closed. 
(e)  No further public hearing on the proposed zoning amendment shall be required prior to the final determination of the city council. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-6) 
Sec. 26-1312. - Final determination by city council. 
The zoning board's role in any zoning decision shall be advisory only. Any zoning decision shall be made by the mayor and city council, which shall either approve or disapprove the proposed zoning amendment. When the public hearing is conducted by the city council at a regular council meeting, action may be taken approving or rejecting the proposal at that meeting, or the council may table the question for consideration at its next regular meeting or a called meeting to be held no later than the next regular meeting. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-7) 
Sec. 26-1313. - Reversionary zoning procedure. 
For a period of 12 months from the date of approval, the zoning board may submit information to the mayor and city council concerning property that has been rezoned and for which no site plan or preliminary plat or building permit has been obtained. The mayor and city council may then review such information, and if considered appropriate, initiate reversionary zoning procedures. Such reversionary procedures shall proceed in accordance with the amendment provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-8) 
Sec. 26-1314. - Limitation on reapplications. 
If the city council shall take official action defeating a proposed zoning amendment that seeks to rezone property, the same property may not be considered again for rezoning until the expiration of 12 months from the date of the official action of the city council. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-10) 
Sec. 26-1315. - Appeal. 
Appeals from the decision of the mayor and city council regarding the adoption or disapproval of a zoning amendment shall be made in the manner provided in this chapter regarding judicial review and as provided by state law. 
(Ord. of 12-2003, § 23-9) 
Chapter 28 - LAW ENFORCEMENT[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Law enforcement generally, O.C.G.A. § 35-1-1 et seq.; compensation of law enforcement officers on commission basis prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 36-30-9; dispatch centers to have trained communications officers on staff, O.C.G.A. § 36-26-19. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 28-1. - Disposition of stolen abandoned and impounded property. 
All personal property seized or abandoned and in the custody of the police department shall be disposed of only in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 17-5-54. 
Sec. 28-2. - Wrecker services; call list. 
A call list of wrecker services is established for police department use. All local wrecker services licensed within the city shall appear on the call list. Any wrecker service located outside the city limits which wishes to be placed on the call list must first purchase a business license under the provisions of this chapter. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 7-1-22) 
Secs. 28-3—28-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - POLICE DEPARTMENT 

Sec. 28-23. - Composition of department. 
The police department shall consist of those officers and employees of those ranks and positions as approved by the mayor and council. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 3-1-1) 
Sec. 28-24. - Responsibilities. 
The department shall be responsible for patrol, traffic control, investigation of accidents, investigation of crimes, apprehension of offenders, court appearances, security of business establishments and for any other matters of public safety and law enforcement as directed by the mayor and council. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 3-1-2) 
Sec. 28-25. - Oath. 
Prior to entering upon the duties of their respective offices, all officers of the police department shall take and subscribe the oath prescribed by the city council. 
Sec. 28-26. - Police chief. 
(a)  The police chief shall be appointed by the mayor, with the advice and consent of the city council, and shall be the chief executive officer of the police department, subject always to the orders and regulations of the mayor and the city council. 
(b)  In the exercise of his duties, the police chief shall have the power to establish and enforce rules and regulations for the government of the members and employees of the department, which rules shall, however, be consistent with this Code, all other resolutions and ordinances of the city, and the laws of the state. 
(c)  In the event of resignation, removal, death, or disability of the police chief, the officer next in rank shall perform the duties of the chief until removal of such disability or until a successor has been duly appointed. 
Sec. 28-27. - Police operations manual. 
The chief of police shall be responsible for compilation and maintenance of a city police department operations manual, copies of which shall be available in the offices of the city clerk and the city police chief. 
Chapter 30 - OFFENSES AND NUISANCES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Municipal home rule, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II; O.C.G.A. § 36-35-1 et seq.; crimes generally, O.C.G.A. § 16-1-1 et seq.; maximum penalties that may be imposed by municipalities, O.C.G.A. §§ 36-35-6, 36-32-1, 36-32-5; additional penalties and bond in certain criminal and traffic cases, O.C.G.A. § 15-21-73; authority to impose community service as punishment, O.C.G.A. § 17-10-1; alternative sentences by municipal courts, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-5; powers of municipal court judges in criminal cases, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-3; jurisdiction of municipal court, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-6 et seq.; nuisances generally, O.C.G.A. § 41-1-1 et seq.; jurisdiction of municipal and magistrate courts regarding nuisances, O.C.G.A. § 41-12-5; misdemeanor nuisances, O.C.G.A. § 41-1-6; placement of posters, signs, and advertisements on public or private property, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-58; abatement of nuisances generally, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-7 et seq.; dogs as nuisances, O.C.G.A. § 41-1-7; unlawful junkyards as nuisances, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-246. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 30-1. - Disorderly conduct. 
It shall be unlawful and disorderly conduct for any person to: 
(1)  Act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, whereby a reasonable person would be placed in fear of safety for life or limb; 
(2)  Place the property of another in serious danger of being destroyed or damaged; 
(3)  Use fighting words directed toward another, who becomes outraged and thus creates turmoil; 
(4)  Violently interfere with another's pursuit of a lawful occupation; or 
(5)  Congregate with others to halt the flow of vehicular or pedestrian traffic and refuse to clear the way when ordered by lawful authority to do so. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-1-1) 
State Law reference— Similar provision, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-39. 
Sec. 30-2. - Public drunkenness. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to be on the streets of the city or in any public place in an intoxicated condition. 
(Comp. Ords. 1998, § 9-1-2) 
State Law reference— Similar provision, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-41. 
Sec. 30-3. - Noise; creating unnecessary noise. 
(a)  The creating of any unreasonably loud, disturbing and unnecessary noise within the limits of the city is prohibited. Noise of such character, intensity or duration as to be detrimental to the life or health of any individual, or in disturbance of the public peace and welfare, is prohibited. 
(b)  The following acts, among others, are declared to be loud, disturbing and unnecessary noises and noises in violation of this section, but this enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive, namely: 
(1)  Horns. The sounding of any horn or signal device on any automobile, motorcycle, bus or other vehicle, while not in motion except as a danger signal if another vehicle is approaching apparently out of control, or, if in motion, only as a danger signal; the creation by means of any such signal device of any unreasonably loud or harsh sound or the sounding of that device for an unnecessary or unreasonable period of time. 
(2)  Musical instruments. The playing of any radio, phonograph or any musical instrument in such a manner or with such volume, particularly during the hours between 12:00 midnight and 7:00 a.m., as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of persons in any office, hospital or in any dwelling, hotel or other type of residence, or any persons in the vicinity, except this section shall not apply to schools of music between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. 
(3)  Voices . Yelling, shouting, hooting, whistling or singing on the public streets, particularly between the hours of 12:00 midnight and 7:00 a.m., or at any time or place so as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of persons in any hospital, dwelling, hotel or other type of residence, or any persons in the vicinity. 
(4)  Noisy vehicle. The use of any automobile, motorcycle or vehicle so out of repair, so loaded or in any manner as to create loud and unnecessary grating, grinding or rattling, or other noise. 
(5)  Steam whistles. The blowing of any steam whistle attached to any stationary boiler, except to give notice of the time to begin or stop work, or as a warning of fire or danger, or upon request of the proper city authority. 
(6)  Exhausts. To discharge into the open air the exhaust of any stationary steam engine, stationary internal combustion engine, motor vehicle or motorboat engine, except through a muffler or other device which will effectively prevent loud or explosive noises therefrom. 
(7)  Construction work. The erection (including excavating), demolition, alteration or repair of any building in any residential district or section, the excavation of streets and highways in any residential district or section, other than between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. on weekdays except in cases of urgent necessity, and then only with a permit from the city, which permit may be granted for a period not to exceed 60 days while the emergency continues. 
(8)  Noise near institutions requiring quiet . The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to any school, institution of learning, church or court while the same are in session, or adjacent to any hospital, which unreasonably interferes with the workings or sessions thereof. 
(9)  Loudspeakers on vehicles. The use of mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on trucks or other moving or standing vehicles for advertising or other purposes.
